Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Selling Wheat in Ears and Beans in Pods: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute with Imam Shafi'i on selling grains in natural coverings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on selling grains in their natural coverings and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument by comparing their respective proofs.

Core Idea
Grains in their natural coverings are permissible to sell because they are valuable property known by sight.

This passage presents a clear disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over a common agricultural transaction: selling wheat still in the ear, or beans in their pods. Understanding each school's evidence is essential to see why the rulings differ, and it illustrates how qiyas (analogy) can lead to different conclusions depending on the chosen original case.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa and his school: selling wheat in ears, beans in pods, rice, sesame, and similar items is permissible.
The Hanafi school extends this to all grains in natural coverings.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits selling green beans, walnuts, almonds, pistachios in their husks, and has two opinions on wheat in ears.
Shafi'i's position is based on the covering having no benefit, leading to gharar.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Analyze the Shafi'i qiyas: selling grains in coverings is like selling goldsmith's dust (turāb al-ṣāghah) for its own kind, which is invalid due to unknown quantity and potential ribā.
The Shafi'i argue that the covering conceals the actual quantity, creating gharar.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
Study the Hanafi evidence: a hadith that forbids selling dates and ears before ripening (implying permissibility after), and qiyas to barley (which is also sold in ears). The common factor (jāmiʿ) is that both are māl mutaqawwim.
The Hanafis distinguish the covering from goldsmith's dust because the grain is known by sight and the covering does not render the object unknown.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, these sales are valid; under Shafi'i law, they are generally invalid (with some exceptions for wheat). A buyer or seller must follow the mufta bihi ruling of their school.
This difference affects everyday agricultural trade in Muslim communities.

ويجوز بيع الحنطة فى سنبلها والباقلى فى قشره وكذا الارز والسمسم وقال الشافعي لا يجوز بيع الباقلى الاخضر و كذا الجوز واللوز والفستق في قشره الأول عنده وله فى بيع السنبلة قولان وعندنا يجوز ذالك كله له ان المعقود عليه مستور بما لا منفعة له فيه فاشبه تراب الصاغة اذا بيع بجنسه ولنا ماروى عن النبي عليه السلام انه نهى عن بيع النخل حتى يزهى وعن بيع السنبل حتى يبيض ويا من العاهة ولانه حب منتفع به فيجوز بيعه في سنبله كالشعير والجامع كونه مالا متقوما بخلاف تراب الصاغه لانه انما لايجوز بيعه بجنسه لاحتمال الربا حتى لو باعه بخلاف جنسه جازوفی مسئلتنا لو باعه بجنسه لا يجوز ايضا لشبهة الربوا لانه لایدرى قدر مافى السنابل. ترجمہ اور گندم کا اس کی بالوں میں اور لوہے کا اس کی پھلی میں بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہی حکم چاول اور تل کا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ سبز لوبیے کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہی حکم بادام، پستہ اور اخروٹ کا اس کے موٹے چھلکے میں ہے۔ اور بالیوں میں گندم فروخت کرنے کے بارے میں امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ سب جائز ہیں۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ ایسی چیز کے اندر مستور ہے جس میں کوئی نفع نہیں ہے تو زرگروں کی راکھ کے مشابہ ہوگی جبکہ اپنی جنس کے عوض فروخت کی جائے اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ آپ نے کھجور کا درخت بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ رنگ پکڑلے اور بالیاں فروخت کرنے سے یہاں تک کہ سفید پڑ جائیں اور آفت سے محفوظ ہو جائیں۔ اور اس لئے کہ گندم ایسا اناج ہے جس سے نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے تو اس کی بیج بھی اپنی بالیوں میں جائز ہے۔ جیسے جو کی بیع اور جامع ان میں سے ہر ایک کا مال متقوم ہونا ہے۔ برخلاف سناروں کی راکھ کے اس لئے کہ اس کا اپنی جنس کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے حتی کہ اگر اس کو خلاف جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو تو جائز ہے اس مسئلے میں اگر اس کو اپنی جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو تو بھی شہبند ربوا کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بالیوں میں گندم کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے۔
It is permissible to sell wheat in its ears, and beans in their pods, and likewise rice and sesame. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible to sell green beans, and likewise walnuts, almonds, and pistachios in their outer husks according to him. He has two opinions regarding selling ears of wheat. According to us, all of these are permissible. His evidence: The subject of the contract is covered by something that has no benefit in it, so it resembles goldsmiths' dust when sold for its own kind. Our evidence: What is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he forbade selling dates until they ripen, and selling ears until they become white and safe from blight. Also because wheat is a beneficial grain, so selling it in its ear is permissible, like barley. The common factor (jāmiʿ) is that each is valuable property (māl mutaqawwim), unlike goldsmiths' dust, which is not permissible to sell for its own kind due to the possibility of ribā—so much so that if sold for a different kind, it is permissible. In our issue, if sold for its own kind, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of ribā because one does not know the quantity of wheat in the ears. Translation: And selling wheat in its ears and beans in their pods is permissible. The same ruling applies to rice and sesame. Imam Shafi'i said: Selling green beans is not permissible, and according to him the same ruling applies to almonds, pistachios, and walnuts in their outer husks. Regarding selling wheat in ears, Imam Shafi'i has two opinions. According to us, all of these are permissible. Imam Shafi'i's evidence: The subject of the contract is concealed in something that has no benefit, so it becomes similar to goldsmiths' dust when sold for its own kind. Our evidence: The hadith narrated from the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) that he forbade selling date palms until they ripen, and selling ears until they become white and safe from blight. Also because wheat is a beneficial grain, so selling it in its ear is permissible, like selling barley. The common factor (jāmiʿ) is that each is valuable property (māl mutaqawwim), unlike goldsmiths' dust, because selling it for its own kind is not permissible due to the possibility of ribā—so much so that if sold for a different kind, it is permissible. In this issue, if sold for its own kind, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of ribā because one does not know the quantity in the ears.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the sale of grains still in their natural coverings (ears, pods, husks). The Hanafi position is that such sales are permissible, while Imam Shafi'i prohibits them for items like green beans, walnuts, almonds, and pistachios in their outer husks, and he has two opinions on wheat in ears. Shafi'i analogizes these to goldsmiths' dust (turāb al-ṣāghah), which contains hidden gold or silver particles and is sold for its own kind; such a sale is invalid due to unknown quantity and potential ribā. The Hanafis counter with a hadith from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) that prohibits selling dates and ears before they ripen, implying that after ripening, it is permissible. They also argue that wheat in ears is māl mutaqawwim (valuable property) and thus can be sold, just like barley, distinguishing it from goldsmiths' dust, which is valid only when sold for a different genus. Additionally, they note that if sold for the same genus, the Hanafis also consider it impermissible due to ribā, but that is a separate issue. The text ends mid-sentence, but it was explaining that the quantity in ears is unknown, leading to ribā suspicion.

Key Terms
سنبل (sunbul): The ear or spike of a grain plant, such as wheat, containing the grains.
قشر (qishr): The husk, pod, or outer covering of a fruit or grain, e.g., the pod of beans or the outer shell of nuts.
مال متقوم (māl mutaqawwim): Valuable property that is legally recognized and can be sold; it has value in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider selling wheat in its ears permissible despite the covering?
A) Because wheat is māl mutaqawwim and the ears are beneficial.
B) Because the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) explicitly allowed it in a hadith.
C) Because the covering can be removed easily.
D) Because the sale is by estimation, not weight.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling grains in natural coverings because they are valuable property known by sight, unlike goldsmith's dust.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Selling Wheat in Its Ears: Permissibility and Proof
Hanafi proof with hadith and qiyas against Shafi'i on selling grain in husks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on selling wheat in its ears, state the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the distinction between hiddenness and riba suspicion.

Core Idea
Selling wheat in ears is valid after ripening; the husk is beneficial and impermissibility is due to riba suspicion, not hiddenness.

The permissibility of selling grain while still in its husk was a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson walks you through the Hanafi proof from hadith and analogy, the Shafi'i counterargument from gharar, and the critical Hanafi refinement that separates hiddenness from the true cause of prohibition: the suspicion of riba when selling for the same genus.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its textual proof
Identify the hadith that prohibits sale before ripening, and derive the permissibility after ripening via mafhum mukhalafah.
The hadith is the primary dalil naqli.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its analogy
Understand the Shafi'i argument: the grain is hidden in a useless husk, creating uncertainty (gharar), analogous to goldsmith's dust.
The analogy is qiyas with an asl where sale is invalid.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Note that the Hanafis rebut by showing the husk has benefit (storage), and that the goldsmith's dust case is about riba, not hiddenness.
They prove this by pointing out that selling dust for a different genus is valid.
4
Apply the Hanafi qiyas
See how the Hanafis analogize to barley (permissible by consensus) and use the common illa of mal mutaqawwim.
The Quranic verse (12:47) supports the benefit of husks.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi permits sale for money or other genus after ripening; Shafi'i invalidates it entirely.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text

كتاب البيوع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم
ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ آپ نے کھجور کا درخت بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ رنگ پکڑلے اور بالیاں فروخت کرنے سے یہاں تک کہ سفید پڑ جائیں اور آفت سے محفوظ ہو جائیں۔ اور اس لئے کہ گندم ایسا اناج ہے جس سے نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے تو اس کی بیج بھی اپنی بالیوں میں جائز ہے۔ جیسے جو کی بیع اور جامع ان میں سے ہر ایک کا مال متقوم ہونا ہے۔ برخلاف سناروں کی راکھ کے اس لئے کہ اس کا اپنی جنس کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے حتی کہ اگر اس کو خلاف جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو تو جائز ہے اس مسئلے میں اگر اس کو اپنی جنس کے عوض بیچا ہو تو بھی شہبند ربوا کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بالیوں میں گندم کی مقدار معلوم نہیں ہے۔

امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ یعنی گندم، لوبیا، مغز اخروٹ ، مغز بادام اور مغز پستہ چھلکے کے اندر مختلی ہے اور چھا کا بے فائدہ ایک چیز ہے مشتری کے لئے اس میں کوئی نفع نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی طرح کی صورت میں بیج درست نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ معلوم نہیں کہ چھلکے کے اندر کچھ ہے بھی یا یونہی خالی ہے۔ پس یہ سنار کی راکھ کے مشابہ ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح سنار کی راکھ میں سونے یا چاندی کے ریزے ہوتے ہیں مگر نظروں سے مخفی ہوتے ہیں۔ اور ایسی چیز میں مخفی ہوتے ہیں جس کی کوئی منفعت نہیں ہے یعنی راکھ تو سونے کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو سونے کے عوض اور چاندی کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو چاندی کے عوض خرید نا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ راکھ کے اندر سونا یا چاندی کچھ بھی نہ ہو ۔ اسی طرح چونکہ بالیوں کے اندر گندم اور چھلکے کے اندر لوبیا اور مغز بادام وغیرہ مخفی ہے اور اس کے اوپر کا چھال کا بے فائدہ ہے۔ تو ان کی بیچ بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
احناف کی دلیل ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے کھجور کے درخت پر لگی ہوئی کھجوروں کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں

كتاب البيوع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم
تک کہ ان میں رنگ پڑ جائے یعنی اگر کھجور میں رنگ پکڑ لیں اور پک جائیں تو ان کی بیع جائز ہے۔ اور گندم کی بالیوں کی بیچ سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ سفید ہو جائیں اور آفت سے محفوظ ہو جائیں۔ یعنی اگر پک جائیں تو ان کی بیع جائز ہے۔ یہ حدیث بالیوں کے اندر گندم کی بیچ کے جائز ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے مگر بالیوں کے پک جانے کے بعد ۔ پس جب گندم کی بیع کا اس کے چھلکے میں جائز ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو باقی دوسری چیزوں کی بیع بھی ان کے چھلکوں کے اندر جائز ہوگی۔
دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گندم ایسا اناج ہے جس سے نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے۔ پس بالیوں کے اندر اس کی بیع جائز ہوگی ۔ جیسا کہ جو کی بیچ اس کی بالیوں میں بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ اور قیاس کی علت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ گندم اور جو دونوں میں سے ہر ایک قیمتی مال ہے۔ دونوں سے نفع اٹھایا جاتا ہے۔ پس جب جو کی بیع اس کی بالیوں میں جائز ہے تو گندم کی بیع بھی اس کی بالیوں میں جائز ہوگی ۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ اس کا چھا کا یعنی بھوسہ غیر منتفع بہ ہے تو یہ غلط ہے ۔ کیونکہ بالیوں کے اندر گندم کو ذخیرہ کر کے محفوظ کیا جاتا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے۔ فذروه فی سنبلہ۔ اور یہ بلاشبہ نفع ہے۔ اس لئے بالیوں کے اندر گندم کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔ بخلاف تراب الصاغہ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جوا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سنار کی راکھ کا اس کی جنس کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یعنی سونے کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو سونے کے عوض اور چاندی کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو چاندی کے عوض بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور عدم جواز کی وجہ سے معقود علیہ کا راکھ میں مخفی ہونا نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضرت امام شافعی کا خیال ہے۔ بلکہ عدم جواز کی وجہ احتمال ربوا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر اس راکھ کو خلاف جنس کے عوض بیچا مثلاً سونے کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو چاندی کے عوض یا چاندی کے ریزوں والی راکھ کو سونے کے عوض بیچا تو جائز ہے۔ اگر محض معقود علیہ کا خفی ہو نا عدم جواز کی علت ہوتا تو خلاف جنس کی صورت میں بھی بیع نا جائز ہونی چاہیے تھی ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ معقود علیہ کا خفی ہو نا عدم جواز بیع کی علت نہیں ہے۔ یہی بات اگر ہمارے مذکورہ مسئلہ میں پائی جائے مثلاً گندم کی بالیوں کو گندم کے عوض بیچا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی ربوا کا احتمال ہے ۔ معلوم نہیں کہ بالیوں میں کس قدر گندم ہے اس کے عوض سے کم ہے یا زائد ہے یا برابر ہے۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی کہ جس طرح ربوا حرام ہے اسی طرح شبہ کر بوا بھی حرام ہے۔ پس شبه ربوا سے بچنے کے لئے بالیوں کی بیع کو اس کی جنس یعنی گندم کے عوض بیچنے کو نا جائز قرار دیا ہے۔
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary on Hidayah Volume Eight. Our proof is the hadith narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he prohibited selling the date palm until it turns red, and selling the ears until they become white and become safe from calamity. And because wheat is a grain from which benefit is derived, so selling it in its ears is permissible, like the sale of barley. And the common factor is that each of them is a valuable property. Contrary to the ash of goldsmiths, because selling it for its own genus is not permissible due to the possibility of riba; if it is sold for a different genus, it is permissible. In this issue, if it is sold for its own genus, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of riba, because the quantity of wheat in the ears is unknown. Explanation: 'hattah' means wheat, 'sunbul' means ear or spike in which grains grow. And ours: baqla (broad beans), lubia (kidney beans), jauz (walnuts), lawz (almonds), fustuq (pistachios), chaval (rice), jumaym til (sesame). The ruling: selling wheat in its ears, and broad beans in their pods, and similarly rice in its husk, and sesame in its hull is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i said: the sale of green broad beans in their pods is not permissible; similarly, selling walnuts, almonds, and pistachios in their first husk is not permissible. Regarding the sale of wheat in its ears, there are two opinions from Imam al-Shafi'i: one of permissibility and the other of non-permissibility. In our view, the sale of all these is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: The subject matter (wheat, broad beans, walnut kernels, almond kernels, pistachio kernels) is hidden inside the husk, and the husk is a useless thing with no benefit for the buyer. In such a case, the sale is not valid because it is unknown whether there is anything inside the husk or it is empty. Thus it resembles the ash of goldsmiths: just as the ash containing gold or silver particles is invisible and the ash itself has no benefit, so selling such ash for gold or silver is not permissible because there might be no gold or silver inside. Similarly, since the wheat in the ears and the beans in the pods are hidden and the outer husk is useless, their sale is not permissible. The Hanafi proof: Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling dates on the tree until they turn red (i.e., ripen), and prohibited selling wheat in the ears until they become white and safe from calamity (i.e., ripened). This hadith indicates the permissibility of selling wheat in the ears after they ripen. Once the permissibility of selling wheat in its husk is established, the sale of other similar items in their husks is also permissible. The second rational proof: Wheat is a grain from which benefit is derived, so its sale in the ears is permissible, just as the sale of barley in its ears is unanimously permissible. The common effective cause (illa) is that both wheat and barley are valuable property from which benefit is derived. So when selling barley in its ears is permissible, selling wheat in its ears is also permissible. As for the objection that the husk (straw) is useless, this is incorrect because wheat is stored and preserved in the ears; Allah says: 'Leave it in its ears' (Quran 12:47). This is undoubtedly a benefit. Therefore, the sale of wheat in the ears is permissible. Contrary to the analogy with the goldsmith's dust: the response is that selling goldsmith's dust for its own genus is not permissible due to the possibility of riba, not because the subject matter is hidden. If it is sold for a different genus, it is permissible. If hiddenness were the cause, it would also be impermissible when sold for a different genus, but that is not the case. Thus hiddenness is not the cause of impermissibility. In our issue, if wheat ears are sold for wheat (same genus), it is also impermissible due to the possibility of riba, because it is unknown whether the wheat in the ears is more, less, or equal to the price. Just as riba is forbidden, so is the suspicion of riba. To avoid the suspicion of riba, selling ears for their own genus (wheat) is declared impermissible.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of grain and nuts while they are still in their husks or pods. The Hanafi position is that once the grains are ripe (e.g., wheat turns white, dates turn red), selling them in their natural coverings is permissible. Imam Shafi'i's view is that such sales are not permissible because the actual commodity is hidden, making the contract uncertain, analogous to selling goldsmith's dust where the precious metal is concealed in useless ash. The Hanafi rebuttal relies on a hadith that explicitly permits the sale of dates on the tree once they ripen and wheat in the ears once they turn white. Furthermore, the Hanafis argue by analogy with barley, which is universally allowed to be sold in its ears. The common factor (illa) is that both are valuable grains. They also note that the husks are beneficial for storage, as indicated by the Quranic verse. The Hanafis refine the analogy with goldsmith's dust: impermissibility there is due to riba suspicion when sold for the same genus, not hiddenness. This is evidenced by the fact that selling such dust for a different genus is permissible. Similarly, selling wheat ears for wheat is impermissible to avoid riba suspicion, but selling them for another commodity is permissible. The passage underscores the Hanafi principle that benefit (manfa'ah) is a key consideration, and that hiddenness alone does not invalidate a sale if the benefit is clear.

Key Terms
سنبل (sunbul): An ear or spike of grain containing the seeds
ربوا (ribā): Usury or interest; specifically in sales, any excess without compensation
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Valuable property recognized by Shari'ah, from which benefit is permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, selling wheat in its ears is permissible under which condition?
A) Only if it is sold for a different genus
B) At any time, regardless of ripeness
C) Only after it has ripened (turned white)
D) Only if the sale is for immediate delivery

Key Takeaway
Selling wheat in its ears is permissible after ripening, provided it is not sold for the same genus to avoid riba suspicion.

Keys Included in the Sale of a House
Hanafi ruling that keys follow the sale of locks on a house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the inclusion of keys in the sale of a house and distinguish between built-in locks and detachable padlocks.

Core Idea
Keys to built-in locks are automatically part of a house sale; detachable padlocks are not.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a practical question in real estate transactions: when a house is sold, are its keys included? The ruling clarifies that keys follow the locks, and the type of lock determines inclusion. Understanding this distinction prevents disputes between buyer and seller.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling a house. The ruling: keys of the locks are automatically included in the sale.
This is a fiqh ruling on the scope of what is sold.
2
Understand the reasoning
Locks are fixtures attached for permanence, so they are part of the house. Keys are essential for utility, so they are considered part of the lock.
The key is like a part of the lock without which the lock is useless.
3
Distinguish lock types
Built-in locks (hadami) are fixed to the door; detachable padlocks (qufl) are not. Only built-in locks are included automatically.
Detachable padlocks are not fixtures and require explicit mention.
4
Apply the ruling
In a sale contract, if the lock is built-in, the keys automatically transfer to the buyer. If the lock is detachable, the keys are not included unless specified.
This is a default rule; parties can agree otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گھر کی بیع میں اس گھر کی چابیاں بھی داخل ہیں
ومن باع دار ادخل فى البيع مفاتيح اغلاقها لانه يدخل فيه الاغلاق لانها مركبة فيها للبقاء والمفتاح يدخل في بيع الغلق من غير تسمية لانه بمنزلة بعض منه اذ لا ينتفع به بدونه
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے کوئی مکان خریدا تو اس کے نالوں کی چابیاں بھی بیج میں داخل ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ تالے بیچ میں داخل ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ تالے اس میں باقی رہنے کے واسطے جڑے ہوتے ہیں۔ اور تالے کی بیع میں اس کی کنجی بغیر ذکر کے داخل ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ کنجی تالے کے جز کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ بغیر کنجی کے تالے سے نفع نہیں اٹھایا جاسکتا ہے۔
تشریح اور تالے دو طرح کے ہوتے ہیں ایک تو وہ جو دروازوں کے ساتھ جڑ دیئے جاتے ہیں جنکو ہضمی تالے کہتے ہیں۔ دوسرے جن کو قفل کہتے ہیں۔ ان کو کنڈے میں ڈال کر بند کیا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں ہضمی تالے مراد ہیں۔
The keys of a house are also included in its sale. Whoever sells a house, the keys of its locks are included in the sale because the locks are included; they are fixed in the house for permanence. And the key is included in the sale of the lock without being mentioned, because it is like a part of it, as no benefit can be taken from the lock without it. Translation: And whoever buys a house, the keys of its locks also enter into the sale because the locks enter into the sale; they are affixed to it for permanence. And the key enters into the sale of the lock without being named, because it is in the position of a part of it, since no benefit is obtained from the lock without it. Explanation: Locks are of two types: one that is attached to the doors, called hadami locks; the other is called qufl (padlock), which is placed on a hasp and closed. Here, hadami locks are intended.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Book of Sales in the Hidayah: when a house is sold, the keys to its locks are automatically included in the sale. The reasoning is that the locks themselves are included because they are fixed to the house as a permanent fixture. The keys are considered part of the locks because a lock is useless without its key. The commentary clarifies that this applies specifically to built-in locks (hadami), not detachable padlocks (qufl). This is a straightforward ruling with no proof cited here beyond the logical necessity of key functioning.

Key Terms
ہضمی تالے (hazami tale): Built-in locks that are fixed to the door, considered part of the house
قفل (qufl): Detachable padlock that is not permanently attached

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following keys is automatically included in the sale of a house?
A) Keys to a detachable padlock
B) Keys to a built-in lock attached to the door
C) Keys to a car stored in the garage
D) Keys to a separate storage shed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, built-in locks are fixtures, so their keys automatically transfer with the house sale.

Selling Wheat in Ears and the Goldsmith Dust Analogy
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on selling grain in husk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows selling wheat in ears for a different commodity but prohibits it for the same kind, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the goldsmith's dust analogy.

Core Idea
Selling wheat in its ears is permissible for a different kind, but not for wheat itself, due to the risk of ribā—the same reason goldsmith's dust is prohibited for its own kind.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the sale of grain while still in its husk. The Hanafi school argues from a hadith and rational analogy that once ripened, such sale is permissible for a different commodity. Imam Shafi'i objects by comparing it to the sale of goldsmith's dust, where the object is hidden. The Hanafi refutation distinguishes the true cause: the risk of ribā, not hiddenness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the Hanafi position
The hadith about dates and wheat ripening implies permissibility after ripening. This is the basis for allowing the sale of wheat in its ears once ripened.
The hadith is cited as evidence for permissibility, not prohibition.
2
Trace the Hanafi qiyas
The Hanafis analogize wheat to barley (unanimously permissible) using the common cause (both are valuable and beneficial). This justifies extending the ruling to wheat in its ears.
The qiyas is based on the shared property of being a stored beneficial grain.
3
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam Shafi'i analogizes grain in husk to goldsmith's dust (turāb al-ṣāgha), claiming the impermissibility is due to the object being hidden (gharar).
Shafi'i argues that buying wheat in ears is like buying gold dust with unknown content.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis refute by showing that goldsmith's dust is permissible when sold for a different kind (e.g., gold dust for silver). If hiddenness were the cause, it would be impermissible regardless of kind. Thus, the true cause is the risk of ribā.
The key evidence is the permissibility of selling gold dust for a different jins.
5
Apply to the wheat case
Selling wheat in ears for wheat is impermissible due to shubhat ribā (unknown quantity risks inequality). Selling for a different kind (e.g., barley) is permissible because ribā only applies within the same jins.
This distinction resolves the dispute: Hanafis allow cross-jins sale; Shafi'is disallow all until threshed.

Source Text

مذکورہ مسئلہ میں پائی جائے مثلاً گندم کی بالیوں کو گندم کے عوض بیچا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بھی ربوا کا احتمال ہے ۔ معلوم نہیں کہ بالیوں میں کس قدر گندم ہے اس کے عوض سے کم ہے یا زائد ہے یا برابر ہے۔ اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی کہ جس طرح ربوا حرام ہے اسی طرح شبہ کر بوا بھی حرام ہے۔ پس شبه ربوا سے بچنے کے لئے بالیوں کی بیع کو اس کی جنس یعنی گندم کے عوض بیچنے کو نا جائز قرار دیا ہے۔
Until color appears in them, meaning if dates take on color and ripen, then their sale is permissible. And He forbade the sale of wheat spikes until they become white and safe from calamity, meaning if they ripen, their sale is permissible. This hadith indicates the permissibility of selling wheat inside spikes, but after the spikes have ripened. So when the permissibility of selling wheat in its husk is established, then the sale of other things in their husks will also be permissible. Another rational proof is that wheat is a grain from which benefit is derived, so its sale inside spikes will be permissible, just as the sale of barley in its spikes is unanimously permissible. And the comprehensive cause of analogy is that both wheat and barley are valuable property; benefit is derived from both. So when the sale of barley in its spikes is permissible, then the sale of wheat in its spikes will also be permissible. As for saying that its chaff, i.e., straw, is not beneficial, that is incorrect, because wheat is stored and preserved inside the spikes, as Allah says: 'So leave it in its ear.' And this is undoubtedly a benefit. Therefore, the sale of wheat inside spikes will be permissible. This is contrary to the analogy of Imam Shafi'i from the dust of the goldsmith. The gist of the response is that selling the ash of a goldsmith in exchange for its own kind is not permissible, meaning selling ash containing gold particles for gold, and ash containing silver particles for silver, is not permissible. And the reason for impermissibility is not that the object of sale is hidden in the ash, as Imam Shafi'i thinks, but rather the reason is the possibility of riba. Thus, if that ash is sold for a different kind, for example, ash with gold particles for silver, or ash with silver particles for gold, it is permissible. If mere hiddenness of the object of sale were the cause of impermissibility, then in the case of a different kind, the sale should also be impermissible, but it is not. So it is known that hiddenness of the object of sale is not the cause of impermissibility. If the same situation occurs in our mentioned issue, for example, if wheat spikes are sold for wheat, then this is also impermissible, because in this case there is also the possibility of riba; it is not known how much wheat is in the spikes, whether it is less, more, or equal to the price. And it has passed earlier that just as riba is forbidden, so is shubhat riba forbidden. Therefore, to avoid shubhat riba, the sale of spikes for their own kind, i.e., wheat for wheat, has been declared impermissible.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The passage begins with a hadith indicating the permissibility of selling wheat in its ears once they have ripened. The Hanafi school extends this permissibility to other grains by analogy (qiyas): since barley in its ears is permissible by consensus, wheat should be the same because both are valuable and beneficial. The text also provides a rational argument: wheat is storeable and benefited from in its husk, and Allah's verse 'So leave it in its ear' (12:47) is cited as evidence of benefit. Then the passage addresses Imam Shafi'i's objection: he analogizes this to the case of goldsmith's dust (turāb al-ṣāgha), where he claims the impermissibility of selling the dust for its own kind (e.g., gold dust for gold) is because the gold is hidden in the dust. The Hanafi response refutes this: the true cause is the possibility of riba (interest), not hiddenness. Evidence is that if the dust is sold for a different kind (e.g., gold dust for silver), it is permissible—if hiddenness were the cause, it would also be impermissible there. Applying this to wheat: selling wheat in ears for wheat is impermissible due to shubhat riba (suspicion of riba), because the quantity of wheat in the ears is unknown, potentially causing inequality. Thus, the Hanafi position allows selling wheat in ears for a different commodity but not for wheat itself.

Key Terms
تراب الصاغة (turāb al-ṣāgha): The dust or ashes from a goldsmith's workshop containing particles of gold or silver.
شبه ربوا (shubhat ribā): A transaction that strongly resembles riba, making it prohibited as a precaution.
ربوا (ribā): Unlawful gain from a sale contract, specifically in exchanges of same commodities with inequality or deferment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject Imam Shafi'i's analogy of grain in husk to goldsmith's dust?
A) Because the hadith says it is permissible
B) Because the goldsmith's dust case is impermissible due to riba, not hiddenness
C) Because barley in ears is sold by consensus
D) Because the verse proves benefit

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between selling grain in husk for a different commodity (permissible) versus for its own kind (impermissible due to ribā risk), refuting the Shafi'i analogy of hiddenness.

Inclusion of Keys in Sale of a House
Fiqh ruling with rational proof on key inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on inclusion of keys in house sale and apply the principle of fixtures to similar cases.

Core Idea
Keys of built-in locks are automatically included in house sale because they are essential parts of permanent fixtures.

When buying a house, what exactly is included in the sale? Hanafi fiqh provides a clear rule: anything attached to the property for permanence (baqa wa qarar) is considered part of the sale. This lesson explores that rule through the specific case of keys and locks, showing how the key is included as a necessary component of a fixture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that keys of built-in locks (hadami) are included in the sale of a house without being mentioned. This is the established Hanafi position.
The ruling applies only to locks fixed for permanence, not removable padlocks.
2
Identify the underlying principle
The principle is that any item attached to the sold property for permanence and stationariness (baqa wa qarar) is automatically included in the sale. Locks are attached to doors for permanence, so they are part of the house.
This principle is a standard Hanafi rule for fixtures (uruf).
3
Trace the analogy for the key
The key is considered like a part of the lock because the lock cannot be used without it. Since the lock is included, its essential part (the key) is also included.
The reasoning is qiyas (analogy): key is to lock as part is to whole.
4
Apply the chain
Key enters through lock, lock enters through house. Therefore, keys are included in the house sale indirectly.
This chain is explicit in the passage.
5
Distinguish cases
Not all locks are included; only built-in locks (hadami) that are permanently affixed. Removable padlocks (qufl) and their keys are not automatically included.
Custom and permanence determine inclusion.

Source Text

The keys of the house are also included in its sale.
And whoever sold a house, the keys of its locks are included in the sale, because the locks are included in the sale, since they are fixed in it for permanence. And the key is included in the sale of the lock without being mentioned, because it is like a part of it, since no benefit can be derived from it without the key.
Translation: And whoever bought a house, the keys of its locks will also be included in the sale, because the locks are included in the sale, for they are attached to it for permanence. And in the sale of a lock, its key is included without mention, because the key is like a part of the lock, since no benefit can be derived from the lock without the key.
Commentary: There are two types of locks: one type that is attached to doors, called built-in locks (hadami); the other type called qufl (padlocks), which are put into a hasp to be closed. Here, built-in locks are meant.
Now the ruling is: if someone buys a house that has built-in locks and cabinets with hasps, then the built-in locks, hasps, and their keys are included in the sale. All these belong to the buyer, whether they were mentioned or not. The built-in locks and cabinet hasps are included because they are attached to the house for permanence and stationariness, and it has passed earlier that anything attached to the sold property for permanence and stationariness is included in the sale without mention. Therefore, built-in locks and cabinet hasps will be included in the sale of the house. And since no benefit can be derived from a lock without a key, the key is like a part of the lock. And in the sale of anything, all its parts are included. So in the sale of a lock, the keys are included without specification. Thus, the result is: keys are included in the sale of the lock, and the lock is included in the sale of the house; consequently, keys are included in the sale of the house.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (rational proof). The passage establishes that when a house is sold, the keys to its built-in locks (hadami) are automatically included in the sale, even if not mentioned. The reasoning follows a chain: locks are fixtures attached to the house for permanence (baqa wat la qarar), so they are part of the house. Keys are essential parts of locks (without them the lock is unusable), so they are included in the sale of the lock. Therefore, keys come into the house sale indirectly. The text distinguishes built-in locks (haddami, permanently fixed) from padlocks (qufl, removable) and notes that only the former are automatically included. The principle quoted: 'Whatever is attached to the sold item for permanence and stationariness is included without mention.' This is a standard Hanafi rule for fixtures (uruf).

Key Terms
ہضمی تالے (haddami taale): Built-in locks fixed permanently to the door, as opposed to padlocks.
مفتاح (miftah): Key; in this context, the key that operates the lock, considered a part of the lock.
بقاء و قرار (baqā wa qarār): Permanence and stationariness; items attached with the intent of remaining permanently.

Wages of Measurer and Tester of Price in a Sale
Ruling on who pays for measuring goods and testing coinage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi narrations regarding who bears the wage of the coin tester and apply the rule that what a wajib depends on is itself wajib.

Core Idea
Measuring is on the seller because delivery is wajib; testing may be on buyer or seller depending on narration.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn addresses the allocation of costs for measuring goods and testing coins in a sale. While the seller must deliver the item, the costs of ancillary services may fall on either party. The Hanafi school records two narrations from Imam Muhammad on who pays the tester, reflecting a nuanced application of the principle that what is necessary for a wajib becomes wajib itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the matn: Al-Quduri states that both the measurer and the tester are paid by the seller. This is the starting presumption.
Note that the matn is not final; it is followed by a dispute.
2
Understand the rationale for measuring
Measuring (kayl) is necessary for delivery (taslim). Since delivery is wajib on the seller, whatever it depends on (measuring, weighing, cubit, counting) is also wajib on him. This is based on the principle: 'ما لا يتم الواجب إلا به فهو واجب'.
This principle is key to many Hanafi rulings.
3
Distinguish the two narrations on testing
For the coin-tester (nāqid al-thaman), there are two reports from Imam Muhammad: (a) Ibn Rustam: seller pays, because testing occurs after delivery and the seller needs to verify the quality of what he receives; (b) Ibn Sama'a: buyer pays, because the buyer must deliver good (sound) coins, and testing determines quality just as weighing determines quantity.
Both narrations are from the same Imam, showing his ijtihad on a detail.
4
Apply the legal maxim
Apply the principle 'what is necessary for a wajib is wajib'. For seller: delivery is wajib, so measuring is wajib on seller. For buyer: delivering sound coins is wajib, so testing might be wajib on buyer (Ibn Sama'a).
The maxim works differently depending on which party's wajib is under focus.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if seller pays, he bears the cost; if buyer pays, buyer bears it. This affects contract negotiations and default allocation of expenses.
In modern practice, parties may agree otherwise, but the default ruling determines who bears the cost if unstated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و اجرة الكيال وناقد الثمن على البائع اما الكيل فلا بد منه للتسليم وهو على البائع ومعنى هذا اذا بيع مكايلة وكذا اجرة الوزان والذراع والعداد واما النقد فالمذكور رواية ابن رستم عن محمد لان النقد يكون بعد التسليم الاترى انه يكون بعد الوزن والوزن والبائع هو المحتاج اليه ليميز ما تعلق به حقه من غيره اوليعرف المعيب ليرده وفى رواية ابن سماعة عنه على المشترى لانه يحتاج الى تسليم الجيد المقدر والجودة تعرف بالنقد كما يعرف القدر بالوزن فيكون عليه
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ ناپنے والے شمن پر کھنے والے کی اجرت بائع پر واجب ہے ناپنے کی اجرت تو اس لئے واجب ہے کہ مشتری کو مبیع سپرد کرنے کے واسطے بیع کو نا پنا ضروری ہے اور سپرد کرنا بائع پر واجب ہے۔ اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب وہ چیز پیمانہ کے حساب سے بیچی گئی ہو۔ اور اسی طرح وزن کرنے والے اور گڑوں سے ناپنے والے اور شمار کرنے والے کی اجرت ( بھی بائع پر واجب ہے ) اور شمن پر کھنے کا بیان جو مذکور ہے وہ امام محمد سے ابن رستم کی روایت ہے۔ کیونکہ ثمن پر کھنا تو بائع کو سپرد کرنے کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ وہ وزن کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور پرکھنے کی ضرورت بائع ہی کے واسطے ہے تا کہ بائع اس کو جس کے ساتھ اس کا حق متعلق ہوا ہے اس کے علاوہ سے ممتاز کرے یا اس لئے کہ عیب دار کو پہچان کر مشتری کو واپس کر دے۔ اور امام محمد سے ابن سماعہ کی روایت کے مطابق شمن پر کھنے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اسی کو کھرے مقرر کر وہ ثمن سپرد کرنے کی ضرورت ہے اور کھر اہونا اس کے پر کھنے سے معلوم ہوگا۔ جیسے مقدار کا اندازہ اس کے تولنے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ پس پرکھنے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کیلی چیز کو کیل کے ذریعہ بچایا موزونی چیز کووزن کے ساتھ بیچا یا من روعات میں سے کسی کو گز سے ناپ کر بیچا معدود کو شمار کر کے بیچا تو کیل کرنے والے اور وزن کرنے والے گڑوں سے ناپنے والے اور شمار کرنے والے کی اجرت بائع پر واجب ہے۔ اسی طرح مشترکی جو شمن دے گا اس کے کھر اکھوٹا پر کھنے والے کی اجرت بھی بائع پر واجب ہے۔ کیل یا وزن وغیرہ کرنے والے کی اجرت تو بائع پر اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ مبیع سپرد کرنا بائع پر واجب ہے اور بیچ سپرد کرنا کیل وغیرہ کرنے پر موقوف ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ واجب کا موقوف علیہ بھی واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کیل کرنا وزن کرنا بائع پر واجب ہوگا ۔ اور چونکہ کیل کرنا بائع پر
He (al-Quduri) said: The wage of the measurer and the tester of the price is upon the seller. As for measuring, it is indispensable for delivery, and it is upon the seller. As for testing, the mentioned [ruling] is the narration of Ibn Rustam from Muhammad, because testing occurs after delivery. Do you not see that it is after weighing? And weighing [is upon the seller]. And the seller is the one who needs it to distinguish that which his right pertains to from others, or to recognize a defect and return it. In the narration of Ibn Sama'a from him, it is upon the buyer, because he needs to deliver good [coins] of determined [quality], and quality is known by testing just as quantity is known by weight, so it is upon him.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: The wage of the measurer and the tester of the price is obligatory upon the seller. The wage of measuring is obligatory because for delivering the sold item to the buyer, measuring is necessary, and delivery is obligatory upon the seller. And its meaning is when the item is sold by measure. And likewise the wage of the weigher, the cubit measurer, and the counter is also upon the seller. And the statement about testing that is mentioned is the narration of Ibn Rustam from Muhammad, because testing of the price occurs after delivery. Do you not see that it is after weighing? And weighing [is upon the seller]. And the need for testing is for the seller to distinguish that which his right pertains to from others, or to recognize a defect and return it. And according to the narration of Ibn Sama'a from him, the wage of testing is upon the buyer, because he needs to deliver good [coins] of determined quality, and quality is known by testing just as quantity is known by weight, so it is upon him. Commentary: The scenario of the issue is that if someone sells a measured item by measure, or a weighed item by weight, or one of the cloth items by cubit, or a counted item by count, then the wage of the measurer, weigher, cubit measurer, and counter is obligatory upon the seller. Similarly, the wage of the one who tests the price that the buyer will pay for its purity or impurity is also upon the seller. The wage of the measurer or weigher etc. is upon the seller because delivering the sold item is obligatory upon the seller, and delivering it is dependent on measuring etc., and the rule is that what a wajib depends on is also wajib. Therefore, measuring and weighing will be wajib upon the seller. And since measuring is upon the seller...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wages of the measurer (kayyāl) and the tester of coinage (nāqid al-thaman). The base text (al-Quduri) states that both wages are on the seller (bā'i'). The reason: measuring is necessary for delivery, and delivery is the seller's duty. This applies to measure, weight, cubit, or count sales. For testing the price (coins), there are two narrations from Imam Muhammad: (1) Ibn Rustam narrates that the seller pays, because testing occurs after delivery (the seller has already received the price in weight but must test to verify quality or detect defects before finalizing); (2) Ibn Sama'a narrates that the buyer pays, because the buyer needs to deliver good coins and testing is how quality is verified, similar to how weight determines quantity. The commentary explains the rule: 'What a wajib depends on is also wajib' (al-wājibu lā yatimmu illā bihi fa-huwa wājib). The passage ends incomplete but establishes the two positions.

Key Terms
الكيال (al-kayyāl): The person who measures the volume of grain or other dry goods in a sale.
ناقد الثمن (nāqid al-thaman): The person who tests coins for purity (gold/silver) to ensure they are of good quality.
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the sold item from seller to buyer; a wajib act upon the seller.

Items Included in the Sale of a House
Ruling on items attached to a house in a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which items attached to a house are included in its sale without explicit mention and apply the principle of permanent attachment to determine inclusion.

Core Idea
Anything attached for permanence is included in the sale — keys follow as parts of the lock.

When buying a house, not everything inside automatically transfers to the buyer. Fiqh provides clear rules based on attachment. This lesson explores a key principle: items permanently fixed to the house become part of the sale, even without mention. Understanding this helps avoid disputes in real estate transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Items Discussed
The passage mentions embedded locks (ہضمی تالے), shelves' pegs (الماریوں کے کھٹکے), and their keys. Note that these are not portable items but fixtures.
Embedded locks are built into the structure, unlike padlocks.
2
State the Governing Principle
The principle: 'Whatever is attached to the sold item for permanence and stability is included in the sale without mention.' This is a general Hanafi rule for real estate sales.
This rule applies to anything that would damage the property if removed.
3
Apply the Principle to Keys
Keys are not permanently attached, but they are essential to the lock. The passage treats the key as a part of the lock because the lock cannot function without it. Since the lock is included, the key follows as an accessory part.
This is an extension of the rule: parts of included items are also included.
4
Confirm the Legal Consequence
All these items belong to the buyer whether mentioned in the contract or not. The sale is valid and complete with these fixtures included.
If the seller removes them, the buyer may claim compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اب مسئلہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر کسی نے مکان خریدا اور اس میں ہضمی تالے لگے ہوئے ہیں اور الماریوں میں کھٹکے لگے ہوئے ہیں تو اس بیچ میں ہضمی تالے اور کھنکے اور انکی کنجیاں داخل ہوں گی۔ اور یہ سب مشتری کے لئے ہوں گے خواہ ان کا ذکر کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو ۔ یہضمی تالے اور الماریوں کے کھٹکے تو اسلئے داخل ہوں گے کہ وہ مکان کے ساتھ بقاء اور قرار کے لئے متصل ہیں اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ جو چیز مبیع کے ساتھ بقاء اور قرار کے لئے متصل ہو وہ بغیر ذکر کئے بیع میں داخل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے ہضمی تالےاور الماریوں کے کھٹکے مکان کی بیچ میں داخل ہو جائیں گے۔ اور چونکہ کنجی کے بغیر تالے سے نفع نہیں اٹھایا جا سکتا اس لئے کنجی تالے کے جز کے مرتبہ میں ہوگی۔ اور کل شئی کی بیع میں چونکہ اسکے تمام اجزاء داخل ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے تالے کی بیع میں کنجیاں بغیر بیان کے داخل ہو جائیں گی پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ کنجیاں تو تالے کی بیچ میں داخل ہوئیں اور تالا مکان کی بیچ میں داخل ہوا تو نتیجہ کے طور پر کنجیاں مکان کی بیع میں داخل ہو جائیں گی۔
Now the issue is that if someone bought a house and there are embedded locks and shelves with pegs, then in this sale, the embedded locks and pegs and their keys are included. And all these belong to the buyer whether they were mentioned or not. The embedded locks and shelves' pegs are included because they are attached to the house for permanence and stability. And it has passed previously that whatever is attached to the sold item for permanence and stability is included in the sale without mention. Therefore, the embedded locks and shelves' pegs will be included in the sale of the house. And because one cannot benefit from the lock without the key, the key is in the status of a part of the lock. And in the sale of any thing, all its parts are included. Therefore, in the sale of the lock, the keys are included without mention. So the result is that the keys are included in the sale of the lock, and the lock is included in the sale of the house, therefore as a consequence the keys are included in the sale of the house.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding what is included in the sale of a house without explicit mention. The author states that locks, shelves, pegs, and keys are all included in the sale of a house. The reasoning is that these items are attached to the house for permanence and stability, not for temporary use. The key is considered a part of the lock since it cannot function without it, and thus follows the lock. The ruling applies whether these items were mentioned in the contract or not, based on the established principle that anything permanently attached to the sold item is included in the sale.

Key Terms
ہضمی تالے (hazmi taale): Embedded locks built into the house structure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Portable furniture
B) Embedded locks and keys
C) Crops in the field
D) Tenant's personal belongings

Key Takeaway
Anything attached to a sold item for permanence is included in the sale, and accessories essential for use are treated as parts.

Who pays the measurer and money tester
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who pays the measurer and weigher, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over who pays the money tester.

Core Idea
Seller always pays measurer; money tester's wage is disputed between seller and buyer.

In a sale, delivering the goods requires measuring or weighing, and the seller bears that cost. But who pays the person who tests the quality of the price money? This passage from al-Quduri presents the main rule and then reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between two narrations from Imam Muhammad. By understanding this, you will see how Hanafi fiqh handles practical costs and how ikhtilaf arises even within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon: hiring a measurer (kayyal) or money tester (naqid al-thaman). The ruling is that the wage is wajib (obligatory) on someone. For the measurer, it is clearly the seller. For the tester, there is a dispute.
Focus on the difference between measuring goods and testing money.
2
State the main rule for measuring
Al-Quduri states: 'The wage of the measurer and money tester is upon the seller.' The commentary explains that measuring is necessary for delivery, and delivery is the seller's duty. This applies to sales by volume, weight, length, or count.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position for measuring.
3
Identify the dispute for money testing
For the money tester, Imam Muhammad has two narrations: Ibn Rustom reports the seller pays, Ibn Sama'a reports the buyer pays. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The passage explicitly labels these as two riwayat (narrations).
4
Analyze the proofs for each narration
Ibn Rustom: testing occurs after delivery, so the seller needs to check the quality of the money he receives. Ibn Sama'a: the buyer must deliver good-quality money, and testing reveals that quality. Both use qiyas based on who benefits from the act.
The commentary provides detailed daleel for each.

واجب ہے اور جید ہونا پر کھنے سے معلوم ہو گا جس طرح شمن کی مقدار وزن کرنے سے معلوم ہوتی ہے اس لئے شمن لکھنے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہوگی۔
And the wage of the measurer and the money tester is upon the seller. He (al-Quduri) said: 'The wage of the measurer and the money tester is upon the seller.' As for measuring, it is necessary for delivery, and delivery is upon the seller. The meaning of this is when it is sold by measure. Likewise, the wage of the weigher, the cubit-measurer, and the counter. As for testing (money), what is mentioned is the narration of Ibn Rustom from Muhammad: because testing occurs after delivery. Do you not see that it occurs after weighing? And weighing is needed by the seller to distinguish what his right is attached to from other things, or to know the defective to return it. In the narration of Ibn Sama'a from him, it is upon the buyer because he needs to deliver the good-quality specified, and quality is known by testing just as quantity is known by weighing, so it is upon him. Translation: al-Quduri said that the wage of the measurer and the money tester is obligatory upon the seller. The wage of measuring is obligatory because delivering the sold item to the buyer requires measuring, and delivery is obligatory upon the seller. The meaning of this is when the item is sold by measure. Similarly, the wage of the weigher, the cubit-measurer, and the counter is also upon the seller. As for the statement about testing money that is mentioned, it is the narration of Ibn Rustom from Imam Muhammad, because testing the price occurs after delivery. Do you not see that it occurs after weighing? And the need for testing is for the seller to distinguish what his right is attached to from others, or to recognize the defective to return it to the buyer. According to the narration of Ibn Sama'a from him, the wage of testing the price is upon the buyer because he needs to deliver the good-quality specified, and goodness is known by testing just as quantity is known by weighing. Therefore, the testing wage is upon the buyer. Explanation: The scenario is that if someone sold a measured item by measure, a weighed item by weight, or an item measured by cubit, or counted items by count, then the wage of the measurer, weigher, cubit-measurer, and counter is obligatory upon the seller. Similarly, the wage of the person who tests the price the buyer will give (for good or bad) is also upon the seller. The wage of the measurer or weigher is upon the seller because delivering the sold item is upon the seller, and delivery is dependent on measuring, etc. The rule is that what is necessary for the obligatory is also obligatory. Therefore, measuring and weighing are obligatory upon the seller. And if he employs someone else to measure, the wage is on the seller. As for testing the price and checking its good or bad quality, the narration from Ibn Rustom from Imam Muhammad is what is mentioned in al-Quduri, that the wage of testing the price is upon the seller. And the narration from Ibn Sama'a from him is that the wage of testing the price is upon the buyer. The proof of Ibn Rustom's narration is that testing the price and checking its good or bad quality occurs after the buyer delivers the price to the seller. Note that testing the price occurs after weighing the price. And after weighing, the need to distinguish good from bad arises for the seller to distinguish the good from the bad to which his right is attached, or to recognize the defective to return it. The proof of Ibn Sama'a's narration is that the buyer is obligated to deliver the good-quality price (as specified in the contract), and goodness is known by testing, just as quantity is known by weighing. Therefore, the wage of testing the price is upon the buyer.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding who bears the wage for measuring goods and testing money in a sale. The author, al-Quduri, states that the seller pays the measurer and money tester. The commentary explains that measuring is necessary for delivery, and delivery is the seller's duty, so the wage is on him. This applies to sales by measure, weight, cubit, or count. However, for testing the price money, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad has two narrations. According to Ibn Rustom, the seller pays, since testing occurs after delivery and benefits the seller in verifying his right. According to Ibn Sama'a, the buyer pays, because the buyer needs to deliver good-quality money, and testing determines quality. The commentary does not specify which is mufta bihi, but the main text (Quduri) mentions the seller's liability, which is the relied-upon position in the school.

Key Terms
کیال (kayyal): A person who measures dry goods by volume.
ناقد الثمن (naqid al-thaman): A person who tests the quality of money (coins) in a sale.
بائع (ba'i'): Seller.
مشتری (mushtari): Buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The buyer
C) Both equally
D) No one

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the seller always pays for measuring goods, but the wage for testing the price money is subject to a legitimate intra-madhhab dispute.

Who Pays the Weigher of the Price: The Buyer's Responsibility
Ruling on wage for weighing the price money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the wage for weighing the price in a sale and explain the legal reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
The buyer pays the weigher because delivery of the price requires weighing.

This short ruling from al-Quduri establishes a clear, practical point in sales transactions: who must pay the wage for weighing the price money? The answer might seem obvious after reflection, but it rests on a simple principle of responsibility. Let's examine the ruling and its underlying logic.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the legal actor (buyer or seller) who bears the wage for weighing the price.
The text explicitly says the wage is upon the buyer.
2
Identify the reasoning
Understand why the buyer bears this cost: the buyer is obligated to deliver the price, and delivery is realized by weighing.
This links the obligation to the necessity of fulfilling a contract term.
3
Apply the ruling
Consider a concrete scenario: a buyer purchases goods for 100 gold dinars. Who pays the person who weighs the dinars?
The buyer pays, as the weighing is part of delivering the price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شمن کا وزن کرنے والے کی اجرت مشتری پر ہے قال و اجرة وزن الثمن على المشترى لما بينا انه هوا لمحتاج الى تسليم الثمن وبالوزن يتحقق التسليم ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور ثمن تولنے والے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ شیمن سپر د کرنے کی ضرورت مشتری کو ہے اور سپر د کرنا تو لنے سے متحقق ہوگا۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
The wage of the weigher of the price is upon the buyer. He (al-Quduri) said: 'The wage of weighing the price is upon the buyer because, as we explained, he is the one who needs to deliver the price, and delivery is realized by weighing.' Translation: Al-Quduri said that the wage of the weigher of the price is obligatory upon the buyer due to the reason we stated: the need to deliver the price is upon the buyer, and delivery is realized by weighing. Explanation: It is clear.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This is a short ruling statement from al-Quduri that the wage for weighing the price money (e.g., coins) is borne by the buyer. The reasoning is that the buyer is obligated to deliver the price to the seller, and weighing is necessary to fulfill that delivery. Unlike the earlier dispute about testing the money (which involves quality), weighing is about quantity, and it is the buyer's responsibility to deliver the correct amount.

Key Terms
وزن الثمن (wazn al-thaman): The act of weighing the price money to determine its quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the seller needs to verify the amount.
B) Because the buyer needs to deliver the price, and weighting is required for delivery.
C) Because both parties benefit equally.
D) Because the Hanafi school always puts costs on the buyer.

Key Takeaway
The buyer bears the wage for weighing the price because weighing is necessary for the buyer to fulfill his obligation to deliver the price.

Order of Delivery in Cash and Barter Sales
Ruling on delivery order in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of delivery in cash sales and barter sales, and explain the rationale of ta'yeen (specification).

Core Idea
In cash sales, the buyer pays first; in barter, both deliver simultaneously.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes the default order of performance when a dispute arises in a sale. The ruling is based on the concept of ta'yeen: the sold item is specified at contract, but the price is not specified until possession. This asymmetry determines who must perform first. We will examine the rule for cash sales, then for barter, and understand the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a cash sale (goods for currency) and a barter (goods for goods or currency for currency). Note the ruling for each.
2
Understand ta'yeen
ta'yeen means specification. In a cash sale, the buyer's right is specified in the specific goods; the seller's right in the price is not specified until possession. This drives the order.
3
Apply the rule
If a dispute arises, the buyer must pay first in a cash sale; in a barter, both deliver simultaneously because both items are equally specified or unspecified.
4
Explain the rationale
The order achieves equality: the buyer pays first so that the seller's right becomes specified through possession, matching the buyer's already specified right.

In a sale of goods for a price, the buyer should hand over the price first, then the seller hands over the sold item. He (al-Quduri) said: 'Whoever sells goods for a price, it is said to the buyer: Pay the price first, because the buyer's right is specified in the sold item, so the price is paid first so that the seller's right is specified by possession, since it is not specified by specification, to achieve equality. He said: Whoever sells goods for goods or price for price, it is said to both: Hand over simultaneously, because both are equal in specification and lack thereof, so there is no need to advance one in payment.' Translation: Al-Quduri said that if someone sells goods for a price (dirhams or dinars), then the buyer will be told: Pay the price first. Because the buyer's right is specified in the sold item (since the sold item is specific), so the price is paid first to specify the seller's right through possession, because the price is not specified by mere specification (in the contract) to achieve equality. Al-Quduri said: Whoever sells goods for goods or price for price, then both will be told: Hand over simultaneously, because both are equal in specification and lack thereof, so there is no need to advance one in payment. Explanation: The scenario is that if someone sold his goods for a price, i.e., dirhams or dinars, and the goods are present there, and a dispute arises: the seller says 'Pay the price first, then I will hand over the goods' and the buyer says 'Hand over the goods first, then I will pay the price.' In such case, the buyer will be told to pay the price first. The proof is that in the contract of sale...
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from al-Quduri on the order of delivery in sales. In a sale where goods are exchanged for price (currency), the buyer is required to pay first before the seller delivers the goods. The reasoning is that the buyer's right is already specified in the specific goods, but the seller's right in the price is not specified until possession. To achieve equality, the buyer pays first so both rights become specified through possession. In barter sales (goods for goods or price for price), both parties deliver simultaneously because both items are either both specific or both non-specific, so there is no need to prioritize one. The explanation clarifies that if there is a dispute about who should perform first, the buyer must pay first in a cash sale.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yeen): Specification of an item in the contract (e.g., the goods are specified; the price is not specified until possession).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The buyer must pay the price first
C) Both simultaneously
D) It depends on custom

Key Takeaway
The order of delivery in Hanafi sales is based on specification: in cash sales, the buyer pays first; in barter, both deliver simultaneously.

Who Bears the Cost of Writing the Price in a Sale?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on cost of writing thaman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi transmissions on the cost of writing the price and explain their rational proofs.

Core Idea
The cost of writing the price is wajib, but Hanafi transmissions differ: seller or buyer.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between two transmissions from Imam Muhammad regarding who must pay for the service of writing the price (thaman) after a sale. The two transmissions offer rational proofs based on the sequence of delivery and the need to establish the genuineness of the price. Understanding this ikhtilaf deepens your grasp of how Hanafi scholars derived rulings from underlying rationales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transmissions
Name the two riwayat from Imam Muhammad: one from Ibn Rustam and one from Ibn Sam'ah. State who bears the fee in each.
2
State the ruling of each
Ibn Rustam's transmission: the fee for writing the price is on the seller. Ibn Sam'ah's transmission: the fee is on the buyer.
3
Analyse the proof of Ibn Rustam's transmission
Follow the rational argument: the need to write arises after the buyer delivers the price to the seller. The seller then needs to verify genuineness to protect his right or to return defective coins. Thus, the fee is on the seller.
4
Analyse the proof of Ibn Sam'ah's transmission
The buyer is obligated to deliver a good price (jayed thaman). Writing and verifying the price helps ascertain its goodness, analogous to weighing for quantity. Therefore, the fee is on the buyer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجب ہو تو اگر اس نے دوسرے سے کیل کرایا تو اس کی اجرت بھی بائع پر واجب ہوگی اور ثمن کو پرکھنا اور اس کے کھرے کھوٹے کو دیکھنا تو امام محمد سے ابن رستم کی روایت تو وہی ہے جو قدوری میں مذکور ہے کہ ثمن پر لکھنے کی اجرت بائع پر واجب ہے اور امام محمد سے ابن سماعہ کی روایت یہ ہے کہ ثمن پر لکھنے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہے ابن رستم کی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثمن پر لکھنا اور اس کا کھرا کھوٹا ہونا دیکھنا اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب کہ مشتری ثمن بائع کو سپرد کر دے۔ چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ ثمن پر لکھنا ثمن وزن کرنے کے بعد ہو گا۔ اور ثمن وزن کرنے سے تعیین تحقیق ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ ثمن پر لکھنے کی ضرورت تسلیم کے بعد ہی پیش آئے گی ۔ اور تسلیم ثمن کے بعد کھرا کھوٹا پہچاننے کی ضرورت بائع کو ہے تا کہ بائع کھرے کو جس سے اس کا حق متعلق ہے کھوٹے سے ممتاز کر سکے ۔ یا اس لئے کہ عیب دار کو پہچان کر مشتری کو واپس کر دے۔ اور ابن سماعہ کی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری پر چونکہ جید ثمن ( جو عقد بیع میں متعین کیا گیا ہے ) سپرد کرنا واجب ہے اور جید ہونا پر کھنے سے معلوم ہو گا جس طرح ثمن کی مقدار وزن کرنے سے معلوم ہوتی ہے اس لئے ثمن لکھنے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہوگی۔
If it is obligatory, then if he had someone else measure, his fee will also be obligatory on the seller. As for testing the price and seeing its genuine and counterfeit, there is a transmission from Imam Muhammad from Ibn Rustam which is what is mentioned in al-Quduri: that the fee for writing the price is obligatory on the seller. And there is a transmission from Imam Muhammad from Ibn Sam'ah that the fee for writing the price is obligatory on the buyer. The proof of Ibn Rustam's transmission is that writing the price and checking its genuineness occurs when the buyer hands over the price to the seller. So you observe that writing the price will be after weighing the price. And by weighing the price, determination (ta'yin) and verification are achieved. So it is established that the need to write the price will arise only after delivery. And after delivery of the price, the need to recognize genuine and counterfeit is for the seller, so that the seller can distinguish the genuine, to which his right pertains, from the counterfeit. Or so that he can recognize the defective one and return it to the buyer. And the proof of Ibn Sam'ah's transmission is that the buyer is obligated to hand over a good price (which was specified in the sales contract), and its goodness will be known by writing, just as the quantity of the price is known by weighing. Therefore, the fee for writing the price is obligatory on the buyer.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding who bears the cost of writing the price (thaman) in a sale. Two transmissions from Imam Muhammad are cited, each with its own rational proof. Ibn Rustam's transmission holds that the fee is on the seller, reasoning that the need to write arises after the buyer delivers the price, and the seller needs to verify the genuineness of coins to protect his right. Ibn Sam'ah's transmission holds that the fee is on the buyer, because the buyer is obligated to deliver a good price, and writing helps ascertain its quality, analogous to weighing. The text does not explicitly give a tarjih (preferred ruling), but the fact that both are attributed to Imam Muhammad indicates an acknowledged difference within the school.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale, whether coins (dirhams/dinars) or other currency.
اجرت (ujrah): Fee or compensation for a service, here for writing or weighing the price.

Fee for weighing the price is on the buyer
Ruling from Quduri with proof on weighing fee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the cost of weighing the price and explain the proof based on the buyer's obligation to deliver.

Core Idea
The cost of weighing the price falls on the buyer because he is obligated to deliver it.

In a sale, there are various ancillary costs beyond the price itself. One common question is who bears the expense of weighing the price (thaman) to determine its quantity. This lesson presents the clear Hanafi ruling from Al-Quduri's matn, grounded in a rational proof: the buyer is the party obligated to deliver the price, and weighing is a necessary means to fulfill that obligation. Therefore, the weighing fee is wajib on the buyer.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Clearly articulate the Hanafi position: the fee for weighing the price is upon the buyer.
This is a straightforward ruling from the matn.
2
Identify the obligation (hukm)
Recognize that the fee is classified as wajib (obligatory) on the buyer, not merely recommended or optional.
Wajib means the buyer must pay; if he fails, he is liable for the cost.
3
Explain the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: the buyer needs to deliver the price to complete the sale, and delivery is verified by weighing. Therefore, the expense of weighing is a necessary part of fulfilling his obligation.
This is a qiyas (analogical) proof based on the general principle that one bears the costs of fulfilling one's own obligations.
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
While the Hanafi school places the fee on the buyer, some other schools may place it on the seller. Understand that this is a valid area of ikhtilaf.
The source does not detail opposing views, but the status is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text

ترجمہ: قدوری نے کہا اور ثمن تولنے والے کی اجرت مشتری پر واجب ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی کہ ثمن سپرد کرنے کی ضرورت مشتری کو ہے اور سپرد کرنا تولنے سے متحقق ہوگا۔

Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the fee for the weigher of the price is obligatory on the buyer, due to the proof we have mentioned: that the need to hand over the price is on the buyer, and handing over is realized by weighing. The proof is rational: the buyer is the party obligated to deliver the price, and delivery is achieved through weighing; therefore, the expense of weighing falls on him. The commentary simply confirms this as clear.
