Fifth example: And among them is that if the buyer takes possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, then deposits it with the seller, and it perishes in his hand during the period, it perishes from the property of the seller because the possession is lifted by the return, due to lack of ownership according to him. And according to the two companions, it perishes from the property of the buyer because the deposit is valid considering the existence of ownership. Translation: Among these issues, one is that if the buyer took possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, then deposited it with the seller, then during the option period it perished in the seller's possession, then it perished from the seller's property. Because by returning to the seller, the buyer's possession was lifted. This is because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer had not become the owner. And according to the two companions, it perished from the buyer's property because, considering ownership for the buyer, his deposit was valid. Explanation: The scenario is that in the case of the buyer's option, the buyer took possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, then deposited it with the seller. Then the sold item perished in the seller's possession during or after the option period. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale becomes void and this item perished from the seller's property. Hence, nothing (price or value) becomes due on the buyer. The proof is that due to the option, the buyer had not become owner; he only had possession. But when he returned the item to the seller as a deposit, his possession was also lifted. So now the item was lost from the seller's ownership and possession. When a sale is lost from the seller's possession and ownership, the sale becomes void and nothing is due on the buyer. So in this case too the sale becomes void and nothing is due on the buyer. And according to the two companions, this sold item perished from the buyer's property. Because according to them, in the case of the buyer's option, the buyer's ownership over the sold item is established. When the buyer's ownership was established, his depositing the item with the seller became valid. And the perishing of the sold item from the possession of the depositee (the seller) is like perishing from the possession of the depositor (the buyer). And if the sold item perished from the buyer's possession, the sale would be effective and the price would become due on the buyer. So in this case too, the sale is effective and the price becomes due on the buyer.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This fifth example discusses a scenario where a buyer with khiyar al-shart takes possession of the goods with the seller's permission, then deposits them back with the seller. The goods perish during the option period while in the seller's custody. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the loss falls on the seller and the sale becomes void (no price due from buyer). The reasoning: ownership did not transfer to buyer during khiyar; the buyer only had possession. By depositing with seller, possession also returned to seller. So the goods were entirely in the seller's domain. The companions rule that the loss is on the buyer, and the sale is valid (price due). Reasoning: ownership transferred to buyer, so the deposit was valid; the seller is merely a depositee, and loss from his hand is like loss from buyer's hand, so buyer bears the risk and must pay the price.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; entrusting property to another for safekeeping without compensation.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking physical control of an item.
شمن (thaman): Price; the monetary consideration in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the sale was conditional
B) Because the buyer was not the owner, so the deposit was invalid and the goods remained seller's responsibility
C) Because the seller committed negligence
D) Because the option period had not ended

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the liability for goods deposited with the seller during khiyar depends on whether the buyer had ownership; Imam says no, Sahibayn says yes.

Option of a Ma'dhun Slave When Price Is Waived
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar of ma'dhun slave after price waiver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a ma'dhun slave retains the option to return goods after price waiver, and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
When seller forgives price, Imam holds slave still retains khiyar; Sahibayn say option lapses.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the khiyar (option) of a ma'dhun slave. When the seller waives the price during the option period, does the slave still have the right to return the item? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. The difference hinges on whether the slave owned the item during khiyar and thus whether returning would be a gratuitous transfer — something a ma'dhun slave cannot do.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: the slave's option remains because he did not own the item during khiyar; returning is refraining from ownership, which the slave may do.
Imam's view relies on the slave's capacity to decline ownership.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the option lapses because the slave owned the item, and returning it would be a gift without compensation, which the slave cannot perform.
Sahibayn emphasize the restriction on gratuitous transfers by a ma'dhun slave.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Compare the two analyses: Imam sees return as a refusal to own (ibtidad al-milk), while Sahibayn see it as a transfer of ownership (tamlik) after ownership has been established. Determine which viewpoint is more consistent with the rules of khiyar and the capacity of a ma'dhun slave.
The key difference is the moment ownership vests during khiyar.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf: under Imam's view, the slave can validly return the item and the seller takes it back; under Sahibayn's view, the return is invalid and the slave remains liable for the price (though the price was waived, the waiver may still stand but the slave cannot return).
This affects the slave's ability to cancel the sale after price forgiveness.

Sixth example: And among them is that if the buyer is a ma'dhun slave, and the seller relieves him of the price during the period, his option remains according to him (Imam) because return is refraining from ownership, and the ma'dhun has the capacity for that. And according to the two companions, his option lapses because when he owned it, returning from him would be transferring ownership without countervalue, and he is not qualified for that. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, his option remains. Because returning is refraining from becoming owner, and the ma'dhun slave has authority over that. Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This sixth example deals with a special buyer: a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted by his master to trade). He purchases an item with a three-day option. During the option period, the seller forgives the price (i.e., tells him he need not pay). The question: does the slave still have the right to return the item? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, because according to Imam, the slave did not become owner during khiyar. Returning the item is simply refraining from becoming owner, which a ma'dhun slave is allowed to do. The companions say no, because according to them, the slave did become owner when he bought. If he returns the item, he is giving ownership to the seller without receiving any countervalue (since price was forgiven). A ma'dhun slave can trade for profit, but cannot give away property without compensation. He cannot make a gift or gratuitous transfer. Thus, his option is void because he cannot validly return the item. The text cuts off, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
ماذون لہ (ma'dhun lahu): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade.
بری کرنا (bari' karna): To relieve or free someone from a debt or obligation; here, forgiving the price.
ردّ (radd): Return; the act of rescinding the sale under khiyar and returning the goods to the seller.

C) Because the slave was not the owner according to them
D) Because the seller revoked the waiver

Key Takeaway
A ma'dhun slave's right to return goods after price waiver depends on whether ownership vests during khiyar: Imam says no (option remains), Sahibayn says yes (option lapses).

Destruction of Deposited Item During Buyer's Option Period
Ruling on destruction of mabi' deposited with seller during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the destruction of a deposited item during khiyar al-mushtari and explain the underlying disagreement about ownership vesting during the option period.

Core Idea
The buyer's liability hinges on whether ownership vests during the option period: Abu Hanifa says no, Sahibayn say yes.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The scenario involves a buyer who, having taken possession of a purchased item under khiyar al-mushtari (buyer's option), deposits it back with the seller for safekeeping. When the item is destroyed in the seller's hands before the option expires, the critical question is: who bears the loss—the buyer or the seller?

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the facts: The buyer took possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, then deposited it back with the seller. The item is destroyed during the option period while in the seller's possession.
The deposit is a wadi'ah arrangement.
2
Identify the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the sale is void (batil) and the buyer owes nothing; the loss is from the seller's property. The Sahibayn hold the sale is valid (nafidh) and the buyer owes the price; the loss is from the buyer's property.
3
Trace the core legal issue
The disagreement stems from whether ownership (milk) vests in the buyer during the khiyar period. Abu Hanifa says no, so the buyer never became owner; the Sahibayn say yes, so the buyer is owner from the moment of possession.
This is a fundamental usul al-fiqh difference within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze each proof
For Abu Hanifa: The buyer had only possession, not ownership. When he deposited the item, his possession ceased, so the loss is from the seller's possession and ownership, making the sale void. For the Sahibayn: The buyer is owner, so his deposit is valid; destruction from the depositee's (seller's) possession is like destruction from the buyer's own, so the sale is effective.
The reasoning is based on the nature of khiyar's effect on ownership.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa's view, the buyer is not liable for the price; under the Sahibayn's view, the buyer must pay even though the item was destroyed in the seller's hands.
This difference affects the rights and obligations of both parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رکھدیا پھر مدت خیار کے اندر وہ بائع کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہوگئی تو وہ بائع کے مال سے ہلاک ہوئی ۔ کیونکہ بائع کو واپس دینے سے مشتری کا قبضہ اٹھ گیا ۔ اس لئے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مشتری مالک نہیں ہوا تھا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری کے مال سے ہلاک ہوئی کیونکہ ( مشتری کے لئے ) ملک ثابت ہونے کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس کا ودیعت رکھنا صحیح تھا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ خیار مشتری کی صورت میں مشتری نے بائع کی اجازت سے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا پھر اس کو بائع کے پاس ودیعت رکھا پس مبیع مدت خیار میں یا مدت خیار کے بعد بائع کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہو گئی تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک بیع باطل ہو گئی اور یہ مال بائع کا ہلاک ہوا۔ لہذا مشتری پر شمن یا قیمت کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ خیار کی وجہ سے مشتری مالک تو ہوا نہیں تھا ۔ صرف قبضہ کیا تھا لیکن جب مبیع بائع کی طرف بطور ودیعت کے واپس کر دی تو مشتری کا مبیع سے قبضہ بھی اٹھ گیا تو اب گویا مبیع بائع کی ملک اور اس کے قبضہ سے ضائع ہوئی ۔ اور بیع “ جب بائع کے قبضہ اور اس کی ملک سے ضائع ہوتی ہے تو بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے اور مشتری پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیچ باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور مشتری پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ مبیع مشتری کے مال سے تلف ہوئی ۔ کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک خیار مشتری کی صورت میں مبیع پر مشتری کی ملک ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور جب مشتری کی ملک ثابت ہوگئی تو مشتری کا مبیع کو ودیعت رکھنا درست ہو گیا اور مبیع کا مودع (بائع ) کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہونا مودع ( مشتری ) کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہونے کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور مبیع اگر مشتری کے قبضہ سے ہلاک ہوتی تو بیع نافذ ہو جاتی اور مشتری پر شمن واجب ہوتا۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی بیع نافذ ہوگئی اور مشتری پر شمن واجب ہو گیا۔
[The buyer] deposited [the item]. Then within the option period it was destroyed while in the seller's possession, so it was destroyed from the seller's property. Because by returning it to the seller, the buyer's possession ceased. This is because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the buyer had not become owner. According to the Sahibayn, it was destroyed from the buyer's property because, considering that ownership was established for the buyer, his depositing it was valid. Explanation: The scenario is that in a case of khiyar al-mushtari, the buyer took possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, then deposited it with the seller. Then the sold item was destroyed while in the seller's possession during or after the option period. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale becomes void, and this property is destroyed from the seller's possession. Therefore, nothing is obligatory on the buyer (neither the price nor compensation). The proof is that due to the option, the buyer had not become owner; he only had possession. But when he returned the sold item to the seller as a deposit, his possession of it ceased. So it is as if the sold item was lost from the seller's ownership and possession. And when a sale is lost from the seller's possession and ownership, the sale becomes void, and nothing is obligatory on the buyer. Thus, in this case too, the sale becomes void, and nothing is obligatory on the buyer. According to the Sahibayn, this sold item was destroyed from the buyer's property. This is because, in their view, in khiyar al-mushtari, ownership of the sold item is established for the buyer. And when ownership is established for the buyer, his depositing the sold item becomes valid, and the destruction of the sold item from the possession of the depositee (the seller) is like its destruction from the possession of the depositor (the buyer). And if the sold item were destroyed from the buyer's possession, the sale would be effective and the buyer would be liable for the price. Thus, in this case too, the sale is effective and the buyer is liable for the price.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of destruction of a sold item that the buyer deposited with the seller during the option period. The author first states the ruling concisely: if the buyer deposits the item with the seller and it is destroyed during the option period while in the seller's possession, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is considered destroyed from the seller's property, so the sale is void and the buyer owes nothing. According to the Sahibayn, it is destroyed from the buyer's property, so the sale is valid and the buyer must pay the price. The commentary then explains the scenario in detail: the buyer took possession of the item with permission, then deposited it back with the seller. The destruction occurs during the option period. Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the buyer never acquired ownership because the option prevents full transfer of ownership. When the buyer returned the item as a deposit, his possession ceased, so the loss is from the seller's side. The Sahibayn argue that the buyer does become owner during the option period, so his deposit is valid, and the destruction from the seller's possession is equivalent to destruction from the buyer's own possession. This difference stems from the fundamental disagreement about whether ownership vests in the buyer during the option period. The passage does not indicate which position is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): An option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A deposit; placing property in the trust of another for safekeeping.
ملک (milk): Ownership; the right of possession and disposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The sale is void and the buyer owes nothing.
B) The sale is valid and the buyer must pay the price.
C) The sale is void but the buyer must pay compensation.
D) The sale is valid but the buyer is not liable.

Key Takeaway
The destruction of a deposited item during khiyar highlights the fundamental Hanafi disagreement on ownership during the option period: Abu Hanifa denies ownership vesting, while the Sahibayn affirm it, leading to opposite liability outcomes.

Option of a Ma'dhun Slave When Seller Remits Price
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar of ma'dhun slave after price forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a ma'dhun slave retains khiyar when the seller forgives the price, and state the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
A ma'dhun slave's right to rescind a sale hinges on whether ownership transfers during khiyar – Abu Hanifa says no, Sahibayn says yes.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school involving a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) who buys an item with a khiyar (option) condition. If the seller forgives the price during the option period, does the slave still have the right to return the item? The answer depends on a deeper question: does ownership vest in the buyer during khiyar? We will explore the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and see how this affects the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Consider a ma'dhun slave who purchases an item with a three-day khiyar. During the option period, the seller forgives the debt (i.e., remits the price). The question is whether the slave's khiyar remains valid.
The slave is ma'dhun – permitted by his master to trade, but not to make donations (tabarru').
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the khiyar remains. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the khiyar becomes void.
Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Trace the root cause of ikhtilaf
The disagreement stems from a fundamental question: does the buyer become owner of the item during the khiyar period? Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes.
This root difference reappears in many khiyar disputes.
4
Examine the dalil of each side
Abu Hanifa: Returning the item is merely abstaining from ownership (imtina' 'an al-tamlik), which a ma'dhun slave is authorized to do. Sahibayn: Since the slave became owner, returning the item is a gratuitous transfer (tabarru'), which a ma'dhun slave cannot do.
Both arguments are aqli (rational).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the slave can rescind the sale and return the item, freeing himself from liability. Under the Sahibayn, the slave is bound to the sale and cannot return the item, so he keeps it (since the price was forgiven).
The practical result is markedly different: the slave's ability to return the item depends on which view is followed.

چھٹی نظیر ومنها لو كان المشترى عبدا ما ذونا له فابرأه البائع عن الثمن في المدة بقى خياره عنده لان الرد امتناع عن التملك والماذون له يليه وعندهما بطل خياره لانه لما ملكه كان الردمنه تمليكا بغير عوض وهو ليس من اهله ترجمہ اور منجملہ ان میں سے ایک مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ( تین دن کے خیار کی شرط کے ساتھ ) خریدنے والا کوئی ماذون لۂ غلام ہو ۔ پھر مدت خیار کے اندر بائع نے اس کو شمن سے بری کر دی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس کا خیار باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ واپس کرنا مالک بننے سے رکنا ہے ۔ اور غلام ماذون لہ اس کا ولی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اسکا اختیار باطل ہو گیا اس لئے کہ غلام مازون لہ جب مبیع کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس کی طرف سے واپس کرنا بغیر عوض بائع کو مالک کرنا ہوا حالانکہ غلام ماذون لہ اس کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ تشریح عبد ماذون لہ وہ غلام کہلاتا ہے جس کو اس کے مولیٰ نے تجارت کی اجازت دی ہو۔ صورت مسئلہ، یہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری ، غلام ماذون لہ ہو اور اس کو تین دن کا خیار ہو پھر اس کو بائع نے مدت خیار میں شمن سے بری کر دیا یعنی شمن معاف کر دیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا خیار باقی ہے اگر اپنے خیار کے تحت بیع رد کر کے مبیع واپس کرنا چاہے تو واپس کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک غلام مازون مبیع کا مالک نہیں ہوا۔ پس اس کا اپنے خیار کے تحت مبیع کو واپس کرنا ہمبیع کا مالک بننے سے رکنا ہوگا۔ اور غلام مازون کو کسی چیز کے مالک بننے سے رکنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اگر وہ بیچ کر دکر کے مبیع واپس کرنا چاہے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ البتہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کا خیار باطل ہو گیا یعنی غلام مازون اپنے خیار کے تحت اگر بیع فسخ کر کے بیچ دا پس کرنا چاہے تو واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک غلام ماذون جو مشتری ہے مبیع کا مالک ہے ۔ پس اب اس کا مبیع کو بائع کی طرف واپس کرنا بائع کو بغیر عوض ما لک کرنا ہے اور بغیر عوض مالک کرنا تبرع ہے۔ اور غلام ماذون لہ تبرع کرنے کا مجاز نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس کو مبیع واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب مبیع واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے تو اس کا خیار باطل ہو گیا۔
Sixth example: And among them is if the buyer is a ma'dhun slave, and the seller releases him from the price within the period, then according to [Abu Hanifa] his option remains because returning the item is abstaining from ownership, and the ma'dhun slave is competent for that. According to them [Sahibayn], his option becomes void because when he owned the item, returning it would be a transfer of ownership without compensation, and he is not qualified for that. Translation: Among these is a case: if the buyer is a ma'dhun slave (with a three-day option), then the seller releases him from the price within the option period, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa his option remains, because returning is abstaining from ownership, and the ma'dhun slave is the guardian of that. According to the Sahibayn, his option becomes void because when the ma'dhun slave became owner, returning it would be making the seller owner without compensation, but the ma'dhun slave is not entitled to that. Explanation: A ma'dhun slave is a slave whom his master has permitted to engage in trade. The scenario: if the buyer is a ma'dhun slave and he has a three-day option, then the seller releases him from the price within the option period, i.e., forgives the price, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa his option remains; if he wishes to rescind the sale and return the item under his option, he can do so, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa the ma'dhun slave did not become owner of the item. So his returning the item under his option is abstaining from becoming owner. And a ma'dhun slave has the authority to abstain from becoming owner of something. Therefore, if he rescinds the sale and returns the item, there is no problem. However, according to the Sahibayn, his option becomes void, meaning the ma'dhun slave cannot rescind the sale and return the item under his option. This is because, in their view, the ma'dhun slave who is the buyer is the owner of the item. Therefore, returning the item to the seller would be making the seller owner without compensation, and making someone owner without compensation is a donation (tabarru'). And a ma'dhun slave is not authorized to make donations. Hence, he does not have the right to return the item. And since he does not have the right to return the item, his option becomes void.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth example in a series of intra-Hanafi disputes concerning khiyar. It deals with a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted by his master to trade) who purchases an item with a condition of khiyar (option). During the option period, the seller forgives the price (i.e., releases the slave from the debt). The question is whether the slave still has the right to rescind the sale. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the slave's option remains because, in his view, the slave did not become owner of the item during the option period. Thus, returning the item is merely abstaining from ownership, which a ma'dhun slave is permitted to do. The Sahibayn, however, hold that the slave's option becomes void because, in their view, the slave did become owner during the option period. Returning the item would then be a gratuitous transfer of ownership (tabarru'), which a ma'dhun slave is not permitted to do. The dispute again hinges on whether ownership vests in the buyer during khiyar. The commentary clarifies the definition of a ma'dhun slave and the reasoning of both sides.

Key Terms
ماذون لہ (ma'dhun lahu): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade.
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous act, a donation without compensation.
رد (radd): Returning or rescinding the sale, exercising the option to reject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does a ma'dhun slave lose his khiyar when the seller forgives the price?
A) Because the slave never owned the item.
B) Because the slave is not permitted to abstain from ownership.
C) Because returning the item would be a donation (tabarru'), which the slave cannot do.
D) Because the seller's forgiveness invalidates the option.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the khiyar of a ma'dhun slave survives seller's forgiveness only if the slave never owned the item (Abu Hanifa), not if ownership vested (Sahibayn).

Khiyar of a Dhimmi Buying Wine and Converting to Islam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on khiyar when a dhimmi buyer of wine converts to Islam, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids the sale; the Sahibayn void the option, leaving the Muslim with wine he cannot own or return.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: a dhimmi buys wine from another dhimmi with a khiyar condition, then converts to Islam during the option period. The central issue is whether ownership vests during khiyar. Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) reach opposite conclusions, each with significant practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the case: a dhimmi buys wine from another dhimmi with a khiyar (option) condition. The buyer then converts to Islam during the option period.
The subject matter is wine (khamr), which is non-salable for Muslims but initially owned by the dhimmi seller.
2
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the sale becomes void (batil). His proof: ownership does not vest during khiyar, so the buyer never owned the wine. After conversion, he cannot become owner of wine; thus the sale is null.
This avoids the buyer being stuck with wine he cannot lawfully hold.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's ruling and proof
The Sahibayn hold that the option becomes void, and the sale is confirmed. Their proof: ownership vests during khiyar, so the buyer owned the wine. As a Muslim, he cannot return it (since that would involve transferring ownership of wine), so his option is dropped.
This leaves the Muslim buyer with wine he cannot own or sell, creating a legal deadlock.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the sale is void and the wine must be disposed of (poured out). Under the Sahibayn, the sale is binding but the Muslim cannot own the wine, leading to a problematic situation.
The Hanafi response argues that Abu Hanifa's view avoids this deadlock.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not specify a tarjih. Both positions are from the founding imams and considered within the school. A mufti may choose based on additional principles.
Later Hanafi works may prefer one view; students should check fatwa collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتویں نظیر و منها اذا اشترى ذمى من ذمي خمرا على انه بالخيار ثم اسلم بطل الخيار عندهما لانه ملكها فلا يملك ردها وهو مسلم وعنده يبطل البيع لانه لم يملكها فلا يتملكها باسقاط الخيار وهو مسلم ترجمہ اور منجملہ ان میں سے ایک مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب ایک ذمی کافر نے دوسرے ذمی سے شرط خیار کے ساتھ شراب خریدی۔ پھر مشتری مسلمان ہو گیا تو صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کا خیار باطل ہو گیا کیونکہ وہ شراب کا مالک ہو گیا۔ پس وہ بحالت اسلام شراب واپس کرنے کا مالک نہ ہوگا ۔ اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک بیع باطل ہو گئی ۔ اس لئے کہ مشتری شراب کا مالک نہیں ہوا تھا پس خنیار ساقط کر کے بحالت اسلام بھی اس کا مالک نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک ذمی کافر نے دوسرے ذمی کا فرسے خیار شرط کے ساتھ شراب خریدی۔ پھر مشتری مدت خیار میں مسلمان ہو گیا تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری مدت خیار میں مبیع کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے ذمی مشتری مدت خیار میں شراب کا مالک ہیکہ اب مسلمان ہونے کے بعد اگر وہ اپنے خیار کے تحت شراب ( مبیع ) بائع کو واپس کرنا چاہے تو واپس نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ اسلام“ تملیک خمر کے لئے مانع ہے۔ یعنی مسلمان کسی کو شراب کا مالک نہیں بنا سکتا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک بیج ہی باطل ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ مشتری مدت خیار میں شراب ( طبیع) کا مالک ہی نہیں ہوا تھا۔ اور اب مسلمان ہونے کے بعد خیار ساقط کر کے اگر مالک بننا چاہے تو نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ اسلام تملک خمر سے مانع ہے۔ یعنی مسلمان شراب کا مالک نہیں بن سکتا ہے۔
Seventh example: And among them is when a dhimmi buys wine from another dhimmi with the condition of khiyar, then the buyer converts to Islam. According to them [Sahibayn], his option becomes void because he became owner of it, and as a Muslim he does not have the power to return it. According to him [Abu Hanifa], the sale becomes void because he did not own it, and he cannot become owner by dropping the option while being Muslim. Translation: Among these is a case: when a dhimmi unbeliever buys wine from another dhimmi with a condition of khiyar, then the buyer becomes Muslim. In the opinion of the Sahibayn, his option becomes void because he became owner of the wine, so as a Muslim he cannot return the wine. In the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale becomes void because the buyer never became owner of the wine, so by dropping the option while being Muslim he still cannot become owner. Explanation: The scenario: a dhimmi buys wine from another dhimmi with a condition of khiyar. Then the buyer converts to Islam during the option period. According to the Sahibayn, the buyer becomes owner of the sold item during the option period, so this dhimmi buyer became owner of the wine. Now after becoming Muslim, if he wants to return the wine to the seller under his option, he cannot do so because Islam prevents making someone owner of wine — a Muslim cannot make anyone owner of wine. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale itself became void because the buyer never became owner of the wine during the option period. And now after becoming Muslim, even if he drops the option to become owner, he cannot become owner because Islam prevents a Muslim from owning wine.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh example, concerning a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state) who buys wine from another dhimmi with a khiyar condition, and then converts to Islam during the option period. The Sahibayn hold that the buyer's option becomes void (and presumably the sale is confirmed) because the buyer had become owner of the wine during the option period. However, as a Muslim, he cannot return the wine to the seller because that would involve making the seller owner of wine, which is prohibited in Islam. So he is stuck with the wine, but since a Muslim cannot own wine either, the ruling is complex. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale becomes void from the beginning because the buyer never owned the wine (since ownership does not vest during khiyar in his view). Even after conversion, if he tries to drop the option to become owner, he cannot because Islam prevents a Muslim from owning wine. So the sale is void, and the wine must be disposed of (presumably by pouring it out). The dispute again centers on whether ownership vests during khiyar.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, paying jizya.
خمر (khamr): Wine or any intoxicating beverage; legally impure and prohibited for Muslims.
تملیک (tamlik): Making someone owner, transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale remains valid but the buyer cannot return the wine.
B) The buyer's option becomes void, but the sale continues.
C) The sale becomes void because the buyer never owned the wine.
D) The buyer can still return the wine to the seller.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and conversion centers on whether ownership vests during khiyar, with Abu Hanifa voiding the sale and the Sahibayn voiding the option.

Rescission vs Acceptance During Option: The Presence Requirement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on faskh vs ijaza during khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of faskh and ijaza during khiyar in the other party's absence, and evaluate the reasoning of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Rescission requires the other party's presence because it causes harm; acceptance is harm-free and valid even in absence.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about exercising option rights during khiyar al-shart. The ruling distinguishes between acceptance (ijaza) and rescission (faskh): acceptance is valid without the other party's presence, but rescission is not, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf disagrees, equating rescission with acceptance. Understanding the reasoning behind this distinction illuminates how Hanafi jurists balance contractual freedom with protecting parties from harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the dispute
Recognize that the passage contrasts two actions: ijaza (acceptance) and faskh (rescission). The dispute is whether faskh is valid when the other party is not present (or does not know).
The text uses 'hadrah' (presence) metaphorically to mean knowledge.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to these two imams, ijaza is valid without the other's presence, but faskh is not valid unless the other is present. This is the default ruling in the matn.
3
State the opposing view of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that faskh is also valid without presence, a view shared by al-Shafi'i. He argues that the option holder is empowered by the other party, so his consent is not needed.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views are from Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf analogizes the option holder to an agent for sale: just as an agent can sell without the principal's presence, so the option holder can rescind. Thus, faskh does not depend on the other's knowledge.
This is a qiyas: faskh is like ijaza in not requiring presence.
5
Analyze the response of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They argue that faskh is an action affecting the right of another and can cause harm (e.g., the other party may have relied on the sale). Therefore it requires the other's knowledge, analogous to dismissing an agent. Ijaza, on the other hand, imposes no obligation and causes no harm.
The key distinction: faskh involves potential harm (darrar) to the other party, so it requires knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شُرط له الخيار فله ان يفسخ فى مدة الخيار وله ان يجيز فان اجاز بغير حضرة صاحبه جاز وان فسخ لم يجز الا ان يكون الاخر حا ضرا عند ابي حنيفة و محمد وقال ابو يوسف يجوز وهو قول الشافعي والشرط هو العلم وانما كنى بالحضرة عنه له انه مسلط على الفسخ من جهة صاحبه فلايتوقف على علمه كالاجازة ولهذا لا يشترط رضاه وصار كالوكيل بالبيع ولهما انه تصرف فى حق الغير وهو العقد بالرفع ولا يعرى عن المضرة لانه عساه يعتمد تمام البيع السابق فيتصرف فيه فيلزمه غرامة القيمة بالهلاك فيما اذا كان الخيار للبائع اولا يطلب لسلعة مشتريا فيما اذا كان الخيار للمشترى وهذا نوع ضرر فيتوقف على علمه فصار كعزل الوكيل بخلاف الاجازة لانه لا الزام فيه ولا نقول انا مسلط وكيف يقال ذالک و صاحبه
He said: Whoever is granted an option has the right to rescind during the option period and has the right to accept. If he accepts without the presence of the other party, it is valid. If he rescinds, it is not valid unless the other is present, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said it is valid, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. The condition is knowledge; he only alluded to presence to indicate that. [His proof:] Because he is empowered to rescind from the side of his counterpart, so it does not depend on his knowledge, like acceptance. Hence, his consent is not required, and he becomes like an agent for sale. Their proof: It is an action affecting the right of another, namely the raising of the contract, and it is not free from harm, because perhaps the other relied on the completeness of the prior sale and acted upon it, so rescission would necessitate compensation for value if destroyed in the case where the option belongs to the seller, or the buyer might seek a buyer for the item in the case where the option belongs to the buyer, and this is a type of harm, so it depends on his knowledge, like the dismissal of an agent, unlike acceptance because it involves no obligation. And we do not say that he is empowered; how can that be said when his counterpart...
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of exercising the option to accept (ijaza) or rescind (faskh) during the option period when the other party to the contract is not present. The matn states that acceptance is valid without the presence of the other party, but rescission is not valid unless the other is present, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that rescission is also valid without presence, which is also the view of al-Shafi'i. The commentary explains the reasoning: The one who has the option is empowered by the other party to rescind, so it should not require the other's knowledge, analogous to acceptance. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that rescission is an action that affects the right of the other party and can cause harm (e.g., the other may have relied on the sale and incurred expenses), so it depends on the other's knowledge, similar to dismissing an agent. Acceptance, on the other hand, imposes no obligation and causes no harm, so it is valid without presence. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 80.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract during the option period.
اجازة (ijaza): Acceptance or ratification of the contract, confirming it.
حضرة (hadrah): Presence (of the other party) or knowledge; used metaphorically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason given by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for requiring the other party's presence for rescission (faskh) during the option period?
A) Because rescission is a form of worship that requires witnesses.
B) Because rescission can cause harm to the other party who may have relied on the sale.
C) Because the option holder does not have the right to rescind without the other's permission.
D) Because rescission must be done in writing.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rescission (faskh) during khiyar requires the other party's knowledge due to potential harm, whereas acceptance (ijaza) does not, because it imposes no obligation and causes no harm.

Dispute on Slave's Right to Rescind Sale with Khiyar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on slave's khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a ma'dhun slave can rescind a sale made with khiyar, and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
A ma'dhun slave's right to rescind depends on whether ownership transfers during khiyar: if it does, rescission is a forbidden donation.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the capacity of a slave permitted to trade (ghulam ma'dhun). When such a slave purchases an item with a stipulated option (khiyar), can he rescind the sale? The answer hinges on a subtle point: does ownership of the sold item pass to the buyer during the khiyar period? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on this, leading to different rulings on the validity of rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A ma'dhun slave buys an item with a condition of khiyar. The question is whether he can rescind the sale during the option period.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave can rescind because ownership is not fully transferred during khiyar; it is suspended. Thus, returning the item is a simple cancellation, not a donation (tabarru').
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that during khiyar, the buyer becomes the owner of the item. Therefore, returning it to the seller would be making the seller the owner without compensation, which is a donation (tabarru'). Since a ma'dhun slave cannot make donations, he loses the right to rescind, and his khiyar becomes void.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that if the slave rescinds, Abu Hanifa considers the rescission valid and the sale cancelled; the Sahibayn consider the rescission invalid and the sale still binding.
5
Reflect on the unresolved dispute
This text only presents the Sahibayn's reasoning. The tarjih (preferred view) is not specified here, so further study is needed to determine the mufta bihi position.

Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 8. So there is no problem. However, according to the Sahibayn, his option becomes void, meaning the permission-seeking slave, if he wishes to rescind the sale under his option and return the sold item, he cannot return it. Because according to them, the permission-seeking slave, who is the buyer, is the owner of the sold item. So now returning the sold item to the seller is making the seller the owner without compensation, and making someone the owner without compensation is a donation. And a permission-seeking slave is not authorized to make a donation. Therefore he does not have the right to return the sold item. And when he does not have the right to return the sold item, his option becomes void.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a slave who has been given permission to trade (ghulam ma'dhun). When such a slave purchases an item with a condition of khiyar (option), the question arises whether he can rescind the sale during the option period. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the slave can rescind because he does not become the owner of the sold item during the option period; ownership is suspended. Therefore, returning the item is not a donation but simply a cancellation of the contract. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that during the option period, the buyer becomes the owner of the item. Therefore, returning it would be making the seller the owner without compensation, which is a donation (tabarru'). Since a ma'dhun slave is not authorized to make donations, he loses the right to rescind, and his khiyar becomes void. This dispute hinges on the nature of ownership during the option period.

Key Terms
غلام ماذون (ghulam ma'dhun): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act of giving without compensation, such as a gift or charity.
خیار (khiyar): An option or right to rescind or confirm a sale within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does a ma'dhun slave lose his khiyar after purchasing an item?
A) Because the slave did not have permission to buy.
B) Because the slave becomes the owner of the item and returning it would be a donation, which he cannot do.
C) Because the khiyar expires immediately upon purchase.
D) Because the seller can refuse rescission.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a ma'dhun slave's right to rescind a sale with khiyar depends on whether ownership transfers during the option period; the Sahibayn consider it a donation, while Abu Hanifa does not.

Dhimmi's Wine Sale with Khiyar After Embracing Islam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the khiyar and sale when a dhimmi buyer of wine converts to Islam during the option period, and explain the underlying reasoning regarding ownership of wine.

Core Idea
Ownership during khiyar determines validity: Sahibayn vest ownership, Abu Hanifa suspends it.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a dhimmi who buys wine with a conditional option (khiyar al-shart) and then embraces Islam during the option period. The core difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) turns on whether the buyer acquires ownership during the khiyar period. This distinction leads to opposite conclusions: under Sahibayn the option is voided but the sale stands; under Abu Hanifa the entire sale is void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
Note that both parties are dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) and the object is wine. The sale includes a khiyar al-shart (stipulated option).
Dhimmi status matters because Muslims cannot own or trade wine.
2
Recall the general Hanafi rule on ownership during khiyar
According to Abu Hanifa, during the khiyar period the buyer does not become full owner of the sold item; ownership is suspended. According to the Sahibayn, ownership vests immediately upon the contract, subject to the right to rescind.
This underlying usul difference drives the dispute.
3
Apply the rule to the scenario of conversion
After conversion, the buyer is now a Muslim. The Sahibayn argue that since he already owned the wine, he cannot return it (as a Muslim cannot transfer wine ownership). So the khiyar becomes void, but the sale remains. Abu Hanifa argues that since he never owned the wine, he cannot become its owner now by dropping the option, because a Muslim cannot own wine. Hence the sale is void.
Both positions treat Islam as preventing tamlik (transfer) or tamalluk (ownership) of wine, but they differ on when ownership was acquired.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Sahibayn, the buyer keeps the wine (though as a Muslim he shouldn't own it; a secondary ruling may apply), and the seller keeps the price. Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is void ab initio: the wine must be returned to the seller, and the price refunded.
The difference affects how the transaction is unwound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Seventh Example: And among them is that if a dhimmi buys wine from another dhimmi with the condition of khiyar, then he embraces Islam, the khiyar becomes void according to the two (Sahibayn) because he owned it, so he cannot return it while he is Muslim. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), the sale becomes void because he did not own it, so he does not become its owner by dropping the option while he is Muslim. So he, in the state of Islam, will not be able to return the wine. And according to Imam Sahib, the sale became void because the buyer did not become the owner of the wine, so by dropping the khiyar, even in the state of Islam he will not become its owner. Explanation: The scenario is that a dhimmi infidel bought wine from another dhimmi infidel with khiyar al-shart. Then the buyer became Muslim during the khiyar period. According to the Sahibayn, the buyer becomes the owner of the sold item during the khiyar period, so the dhimmi buyer is the owner of the wine during the khiyar period. Now, after becoming Muslim, if he wants to return the wine (the sold item) to the seller under his khiyar, he cannot return it because Islam prevents making wine owned (by a Muslim). That is, a Muslim cannot make someone the owner of wine. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sale itself became void because during the khiyar period the buyer did not become the owner of the wine (the sold item). That is, a Muslim cannot become the owner of wine.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents another intra-Hanafi dispute, the seventh example (nazir) in the text. The issue involves a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject in an Islamic state) who purchases wine from another dhimmi with a khiyar condition. During the option period, the buyer converts to Islam. The ruling on the khiyar and the sale differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The Sahibayn hold that during the khiyar period, the buyer becomes the owner of the wine. When he converts, he cannot return the wine because a Muslim cannot make another the owner of wine (Islam prohibits transferring ownership of wine). Hence, his khiyar becomes void, and the sale remains valid (though the wine is now owned by a Muslim, which is problematic). Abu Hanifa holds that during the khiyar period, the buyer does not become the owner of the wine. Therefore, when he converts, he cannot become the owner by confirming the sale because Islam prohibits a Muslim from owning wine. Thus, the entire sale becomes void (batil). The practical consequence: under Sahibayn, the khiyar is lost but the sale might be considered valid (though ownership of wine for a Muslim is not permissible), while under Abu Hanifa, the sale is void from the start.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, who is allowed to practice his religion.
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): Option by condition: a stipulated right to rescind or confirm a sale within a specified period.
تملیک خمر (tamlik khamr): Making someone the owner of wine; prohibited for Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the effect when a dhimmi buyer of wine converts to Islam during the khiyar period?
A) The sale becomes void because the buyer cannot own wine as a Muslim.
B) The khiyar becomes void, but the sale remains valid.
C) Both the khiyar and the sale become void.
D) The buyer may continue the khiyar until its expiry.

Key Takeaway
The difference in ownership during khiyar al-shart (vested vs. suspended) leads to opposite rulings on conversion: Sahibayn void the option, Abu Hanifa voids the sale.

General Khiyar: Rescission in Absence of Counterparty
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rescission in absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on rescission in absence and apply the reasoning to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Rescission of a contract in khiyar can harm the other party; thus it requires knowledge, unlike confirmation.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the rule on exercising khiyar (option) in a sale. While confirming (ijazah) is valid even without the other party's presence, rescinding (faskh) in absence is disputed. Understanding the underlying analogies—agency vs. potential harm—is key to grasping the Hanafi positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of agreement
Both parties agree that confirmation (ijazah) is valid even in the absence of the other party. Understand why: it imposes no obligation on the absent party.
The text states: 'If he confirms in the absence of his companion, it is valid.'
2
State the two Hanafi positions on rescission
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say rescission is invalid unless the other party is present (has knowledge). Abu Yusuf says it is valid even in absence.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, but Abu Yusuf's view aligns with al-Shafi'i.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes the holder of khiyar to an agent (wakil) who can act without the principal's presence. Thus, consent or knowledge is not required.
Key analogy: faskh is like ijazah—both are unilateral acts by an empowered person.
4
Analyze the majority's proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that rescission is a disposition affecting the other party's right and may cause harm (e.g., buyer disposes of item, then rescission forces compensation). Therefore, it requires knowledge, like dismissing an agent.
They also argue the holder is not truly 'empowered' because the other party does not own the power to rescind.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if rescission occurs absent, under Abu Yusuf it is valid immediately; under the majority it is suspended until knowledge, and if knowledge comes after the period, the contract stands.
This affects when the rescission becomes effective and who bears the risk.

The one who has the option can accept or reject the contract during the option period. Acceptance is valid in the absence of the other party, but rejection is not valid in this way. He said: And for whom the option is stipulated, he may rescind during the option period, and he may confirm. If he confirms in the absence of his companion, it is valid. And if he rescinds, it is not valid unless the other is present – according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said it is valid, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i. The condition is knowledge, and by 'presence' he intends knowledge. Because he is empowered to rescind on behalf of his companion, so it does not depend on his knowledge, like confirmation. For this reason, his consent is not a condition, and it becomes like an agent for sale. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that it is a disposition in the right of another, which is the lifting of the contract, and it is not free from harm because perhaps he relied on the completion of the previous sale and then disposed of the sold item, so he would be liable for the value if it perishes when the option was for the seller, or he would not seek a buyer for his goods when the option was for the buyer. This is a type of harm, so it depends on his knowledge, thus it becomes like the dismissal of an agent, unlike confirmation because there is no obligation in it. And we do not say that he is empowered, and how can that be said while his companion does not have the power to rescind? And there is no empowerment in something not owned by the person granting the power. And if a rescission occurs in the absence of his companion and the news reaches him during the period, the rescission is complete because knowledge of the rescission has been obtained. And if the news reaches him after the period has passed, the contract is completed by the passing of the period before the rescission. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The person for whom the option is stipulated has the choice to rescind the sale during the option period and also has the choice to confirm. So if he confirms in the absence of his companion, it is valid. But if he rescinds, it is not valid unless the other is present – this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said it is valid, and this is also the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. The condition is knowledge, and by 'presence' he intends knowledge of the rescission. Abu Yusuf's proof is that the one who has the option is empowered to rescind on behalf of his companion, so like confirmation, rescission does not depend on his knowledge. For this reason, his consent is not a condition, and he becomes like an agent for sale. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that rescission is a disposition regarding the right of another, which is the lifting of the contract, and it is not free from harm because it is possible that he relied on the completion of the previous sale and then disposed of the sold item, so in that case, when the option is for the seller, he becomes liable for the value if the item perishes, or if the option is for the buyer, he will not seek a buyer for his goods. This is a type of harm. Therefore, rescission depends on his knowledge. Thus, it becomes like dismissing an agent, unlike confirmation because there is no obligation in it. And we do not say that the one who has the option is empowered, and how can that be said while his companion himself does not own the power to rescind? And there is no empowerment in something not owned by the person granting the power. And if rescission occurs in the absence of his companion and he receives news during the period, the rescission is complete because knowledge of the rescission has been obtained. And if the news reaches him after the period has passed, the contract is completed by the passing of the period before the rescission.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents a general ruling from Al-Quduri on the exercise of khiyar (option) in a sale contract. The person with the option (whether buyer or seller) may either confirm (ijazah) or rescind (faskh) the contract during the option period. There is agreement that confirming is valid even if the other party is absent (i.e., without his knowledge). However, rescinding in the absence of the other party is disputed. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that rescission is not valid unless the other party is present (meaning he has knowledge of it). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that rescission is valid even in absence, and this view is also attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i. The reasoning involves analogies: Abu Yusuf compares the holder of the option to an agent (wakil) for sale, who can act without the principal's presence. Therefore, the other party's consent is not necessary. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that rescission is a disposition affecting the right of the other party, potentially causing harm. For example, if the option is for the seller, and the buyer relies on the sale and disposes of the item, then later rescission forces the buyer to pay compensation if the item perishes. If the option is for the buyer, the seller might not seek another buyer, causing loss. Therefore, rescission should require the other party's knowledge to prevent harm, similar to the dismissal of an agent (which requires knowledge). Additionally, the holder of the option cannot be said to be empowered by the other party because the other party does not own the power to rescind (only the holder does). The passage also discusses a scenario: if the rescission is done in absence but the news reaches the other party within the period, the rescission becomes effective upon knowledge. If the news arrives after the period, the contract is deemed confirmed by the passage of time before rescission.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract, exercised during the khiyar period.
اجازت (ijazah): Confirmation of a contract, making it binding and effective.
وکیل بالبیع (wakil bi al-bay'): An agent authorized to sell; such an agent can act without the principal's presence.
عزل وکیل (azl al-wakil): Dismissal of an agent; requires the agent's knowledge to be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, why is rescission (faskh) not valid in the absence of the other party?
A) Because the holder of khiyar must have the other party's permission.
B) Because rescission can cause harm to the other party, such as when the buyer disposes of the item and later the seller rescinds, making the buyer liable for the value.
C) Because rescission is a form of worship that requires witnesses.
D) Because the contract cannot be rescinded once it is valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, rescission during khiyar requires the other party's knowledge to prevent potential harm, unlike confirmation which is valid without it.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Rescission of Sale Without Knowledge: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the Hanafi dispute on faskh during khiyar without informing the other party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on rescission (faskh) during khiyar without the other party's knowledge, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Rescission without knowledge is invalid because it causes harm — unlike authorization, which does not.

When a party has an option (khiyar al-shart) in a sale, they may either authorize (ijazah) or rescind (faskh). Authorization is always valid without the other party's knowledge. But rescission is disputed: does it require informing the other party? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: Is the rescission (faskh) of a sale by the party with khiyar valid without the knowledge of the other party (who has no option)?
2
State the two opposing positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the 'two'): faskh is not valid without knowledge. Abu Yusuf: faskh is valid without knowledge (also the view of Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
The mufta bihi is the position of the two.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf draws qiyas to authorization (ijazah) and to a sales agent (wakil). The person with khiyar has authority (taslit) to act on behalf of the partner, just like an agent. Since an agent's acts don't require principal's knowledge, rescission also does not.
4
Analyze the Hanafi two's proof
The two argue that rescission causes harm (darar) to the partner, who may have relied on the contract (e.g., disposed of the item). Therefore it requires knowledge to prevent loss, analogous to dismissing an agent where notice is needed to avoid harm. They reject the premise of delegation because the partner himself does not own the right to rescind.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: If the option holder rescinds without informing, according to Abu Yusuf it is valid immediately; according to the two, it is invalid unless the partner learns before the option period ends. The mufta bihi is the position requiring knowledge.
If news reaches within the option period, the rescission becomes valid by knowledge.

مدت سامان کی فروختگی کی ہوتی ہے۔ پس یہ بائع کے حق میں ضرر ہے۔ بہر حال من لہ الخیار کا بغیر اپنے ساتھی کے علم کے بیع کو فسخ کرنا اس کے ساتھی کے حق میں ضرر اور نقصان کا باعث ہوتا ہے۔ اور ایسا کام کرنا جس میں دوسرے کا نقصان ہوتا ہو بغیر اسکے علم کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے من لہ الخیار کا بیع فسخ کرنا من لا خیارلہ کے علم پر موقوف ہوگا۔ یعنی اگر اپنے اختیار کے تحت بیع فسخ کرنے کا ارادہ ہو تو اپنے ساتھی یعنی اگر وکیل بالشراء ہے تو اس کو ثمن دینا پڑیگا پس جس طرح وکیل کو معزول کرنے کے لئے وکیل کو مطلع کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اسی طرح بیع فسخ کرنے کے لئے بھی دوسرے ساتھی یعنی من لا خیار لہ کو آگاہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ برخلاف من لہ الخیار کی اجازت کے۔ کیونکہ من لہ الخیار کے اجازت دینے کی صورت میں من لا خیارہ کے حق میں کوئی ضرر و نقصان لازم نہیں آتا اسلئے کہ من لا خیار لہ کے حق میں پہلے ہی بیع لازم ہو چکی ہے اور من لہ الخیار نے بھی بیع کی اجازت دیکر بیع کو لازم کیا ہے۔ اس لئے اجازت من لا خیار لہ کے علم پر موقوف نہ ہو گی۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب صاحب ہدایہ نے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ ابو یوسف کا یہ کہنا کہ من لہ الخیار کو بیع فسخ کرنے کی قدرت من لا خیارلہ کی جانب سے حاصل ہوئی ہے غلط ہے کیونکہ من لا خیار لہ بیع فسخ کرنے کا خود بھی مالک نہیں ہے۔ اور آدمی جس چیز کا خود مالک نہ ہو دوسرے کو اس کا مالک کس طرح کر سکتا ہے۔ ہاں ثابت ہوا کہ من لہ الخیار کو من لا خیار لہ کی جانب سے فسخ وغیرہ کرنے کی کوئی قدرت حاصل نہیں ہوئی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر من لہ الخیار نے من لا خیارلہ کی عدم موجودگی میں بیع فسخ کی اور مدت خیار میں اس کو اطلاع مل گئی تو فسخ بھی پورا ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ مدت خیار کے اندر اندر من لا خیارلہ کو فسخ بیع کی خبر پہنچ گئی ہے۔ اور یہی مقصود تھا۔ ہاں ۔ اگر مدت خیار گذر نے کے بعد اس کو خبر پہنچی تو فسخ کرنے سے پہلے مدت خیار گزرنے کی وجہ سے عقد بیع پورا ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ بغیر فسخ کے مدت خیار گذر جانے کی وجہ سے بھی بیع پوری ہو جاتی ہے۔
The book of sales: He does not have the right of rescission nor delegation in what the delegator does not own. And if there is a rescission in the absence of his partner and news reaches him within the period, the rescission is complete due to knowledge of it. And if news reaches him after the period, the contract is completed due to the passing of the period before rescission. Translation: Quduri said: The person for whom an option is stipulated has the choice to rescind the sale during the option period, and he also has the choice to authorize it. So if he authorizes in the absence of his partner, it is valid; but if he rescinds, it is not valid unless the partner is present. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said it is valid, and this is also the saying of Shafi'i. Knowledge of rescission is a condition, and 'presence' is a metaphor for knowledge of rescission. Abu Yusuf's proof: The one who has the option is delegated to rescind on behalf of his partner, so just like authorization, rescission is not dependent on his knowledge. For this reason, his consent is not a condition, and it becomes like a sales agent. The two's (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof: Rescission is a disposal of his right to cancel the contract, and it is not free from harm. Because it is possible the partner relied on the completion of the sale and disposed of the object of sale. If the option is for the seller, the buyer may be liable for the price if the object is destroyed, or if the option is for the buyer, the seller may not seek another buyer. This is a type of harm. Therefore rescission depends on his knowledge. It becomes like dismissing an agent, unlike authorization, because authorization does not entail liability. And we do not say that the one with the option is delegated, because his partner himself does not own the right to rescind. Delegation does not occur in a thing not owned by the delegator. And if the rescission happens in the absence of his partner and news reaches him during the period, the rescission is complete because knowledge has been obtained. And if news reaches after the period, the contract is completed by the passing of the period before rescission. Explanation: In the text, 'presence' is a metaphor for knowledge. The case: The one who has the option (whether seller or buyer) has the choice to rescind or ratify the sale. If he ratifies without the knowledge of his partner without the option, it is unanimously valid. But if he rescinds without knowledge, according to the two it is not valid. Abu Yusuf said it is valid, and this is also the saying of Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. Abu Yusuf's proof: He has the option, so he has the power to rescind on behalf of his partner (the one without option). And anyone who has power from his partner's side, his action is not dependent on his partner's knowledge, like the authorization of the one with option is not dependent on knowledge. Thus his rescission is also not dependent. Therefore the partner's consent is not a condition. This is like a sales agent who can dispose of everything as delegated, even if the principal is absent and unaware. The two's proof: Rescission is a disposal affecting the right of the other party which is a binding contract. Cancelling it causes harm. If the option is for the seller, the buyer may have disposed of the object, and if it perishes, he owes the price which may exceed the purchase price. If the option is for the buyer, the seller may not seek another buyer during that period which is the market time. So harm exists. Therefore rescission must be with knowledge. This is like dismissing an agent where notice is required to avoid harm. Unlike authorization, which does not cause harm. The response to Abu Yusuf by the author of Hidayah: Abu Yusuf's claim that the one with option has power from the partner's side is wrong because the partner himself does not own the right to rescind. One cannot delegate what he does not own. So the one with option does not have such power. The author of Hidayah says: If the one with option rescinds in the absence of his partner and the news reaches him within the option period, the rescission is complete because knowledge was obtained within the period. If news reaches after the period, the contract is completed by the passing of the period before rescission.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute within the Hanafi school (and with other schools) regarding the validity of rescinding a sale (faskh) during an option period (khiyar al-shart) without the knowledge of the other party who does not have the option. The passage is an expansion of a ruling from al-Quduri. It first states the basic rule: the person with the option can either authorize (ijazah) or rescind (faskh) the sale. Authorization in the absence of the other party is unanimously valid. However, rescission in absence is valid only if the other party is present or informed according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that rescission is valid even without the other party's knowledge, a view shared by Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is based on qiyas with authorization: since the person with option is given authority by the contract (as per the condition of khiyar), his action is not dependent on the other's knowledge, just like an agent acts without principal's presence. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) counter with a different qiyas: rescission is a harmful act because it cancels the partner's rights which they may have relied upon (e.g., the buyer may have used the item, the seller may have missed other buyers). Since it harms, it requires knowledge to avoid loss, analogous to dismissing an agent where notice is needed. The commentator also explains that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reject the premise that the partner delegates authority to rescind, because the partner himself does not own the right to rescission. Hence the person with option does not act as an agent. Finally, the passage clarifies that if rescission occurs without knowledge but the partner learns within the option period, it becomes valid; if after the period, the contract is automatically confirmed by the expiry of the option.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): An option or right to cancel or confirm a sale within a specified period.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of the sale contract unilaterally by the party with option.
اجازة (ijazah): Ratification or authorization of the sale, making it binding and removing the option.
تسليط (taslit): Delegation of authority or empowerment to act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is rescission (faskh) of a sale invalid without the other party's knowledge?
A) Because the option is only valid when both parties are present.
B) Because rescission causes potential harm to the other party, so they must be informed to avoid loss.
C) Because the option automatically expires if not exercised in presence.
D) Because the other party has the right to first refusal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, rescission during khiyar requires the other party's knowledge because it causes potential harm, unlike authorization which is harmless and valid without knowledge.

Rescission by Option Holder Without Informing the Other Party
Intra-Hanafi dispute on notification requirement for rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the option holder to inform the other party before rescinding, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Rescinding without notice causes harm; the Hanafi school requires informing to prevent darar.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf on a critical procedural requirement in khiyar al-shart. While the option holder clearly has the right to rescind, the question is whether they must inform the other party. The ruling hinges on the principle of preventing harm (darar), a core value in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf each rule on the requirement to inform the other party before rescission.
Abu Hanifa: informing wajib; Abu Yusuf: not required.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Understand the reasoning: the option holder derives power from the other party, so no notification is needed.
Opposing school is Imam Abu Yusuf within Hanafi school.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author of al-Hidayah refutes: the other party does not possess the power to rescind, so cannot grant it. Also, non-disclosure causes harm.
Harm arguments for buyer and seller are detailed.
4
Consider the analogy with agent dismissal
Just as dismissing an agent requires informing him to prevent liability, rescinding a sale requires informing the other party.
The analogy strengthens the rule that notification is necessary.
5
Determine the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: what changes in practice if one follows Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf?
If rescission without notice: according to Abu Yusuf valid, according to Abu Hanifa invalid until informed.

The Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary on Urdu Hidayah, volume eight. It is derived that the one with the option, since he has the power from the one without the option to annul or enforce the sale, therefore he has absolutely no need to inform the one without the option, whether he enforces the sale or annuls it. The argument of the two parties: The option holder's annulment of the sale under his option is a disposition in the right of the one without the option, and that right is the contract of sale – i.e., for the one for whom the condition of option is not stipulated, the contract of sale is binding. And annulling the sale is removing and invalidating that right, and this is not free from harm. That is, in annulment there is harm for the one without the option: if the option is for the seller, sometimes his partner, the buyer, relying on the completion and enforcement of the sale, disposes of the commodity, and as a result of that disposition the commodity perishes. In that case, the buyer must pay the price, and the price sometimes exceeds the [original] price. And obligating the buyer to pay more than the price is clear harm for the buyer. And if the option is for the buyer, the seller, relying on the completion of the contract, does not seek another buyer for his goods, even though this period might be the time of selling the goods. So this is harm for the seller. In any case, the option holder's annulment of the sale without the knowledge of his partner causes harm and loss to his partner. And doing an act that causes harm to another without his knowledge is not permissible. Therefore, the option holder's annulment of the sale is contingent on the knowledge of the one without the option. That is, if he intends to annul the sale under his authority, he should inform his partner and then annul the sale so that he can protect himself from the impending harm. An analogy is the dismissal of an agent: if someone appoints an agent for buying and selling and then wants to dismiss him, it is necessary to inform the agent; otherwise, sometimes the principal dismisses him, but due to lack of knowledge of dismissal, the agent may conduct transactions, and then the agent would be liable for compensation. So just as it is necessary to inform the agent for dismissal, similarly, for annulling the sale, it is necessary to inform the other partner, i.e., the one without the option. This is contrary to the option holder's permission [to enforce the sale], because in the case of the option holder's permission, no harm or loss occurs to the one without the option, since the sale has already become binding for the one without the option, and the option holder has also made the sale binding by permission. Therefore, permission is not contingent on the knowledge of the one without the option. The author of al-Hidayah responds to Imam Abu Yusuf's argument: Abu Yusuf's saying that the option holder gets the power to annul the sale from the side of the one without the option is wrong, because the one without the option himself does not have the right to annul the sale. And how can a person make another the owner of something that he himself does not own? Rather, it is established that the option holder does not get any power to annul etc. from the side of the one without the option. The author of al-Hidayah says: If the option holder annulled the sale in the absence of the one without the option, and news reached him within the option period, then the annulment is complete, because the news of the annulment reached the one without the option within the option period, and that was the purpose. Yes, if the news reached him after the option period had passed, then before the annulment, the contract was already completed due to the passage of the option period, because even without annulment, the sale is completed by the passage of the option period.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding whether the holder of a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) must inform the other party before rescinding the sale. The text presents Abu Hanifa's position (supported by the author of al-Hidayah) that notification is required to prevent harm to the other party. It explains that if the seller has the option, the buyer may have disposed of the goods relying on the sale's completion, and if the seller rescinds without notice, the buyer could be liable for the price if the goods perish. Similarly, if the buyer has the option, the seller may have foregone other opportunities. Thus, to avoid harm, the option holder must inform the other party. The text analogizes this to the dismissal of an agent, where informing the agent is necessary to prevent unauthorized transactions. It then refutes Abu Yusuf's argument that the option holder derives power from the other party, pointing out that the other party does not possess the power to rescind themselves, so cannot grant it. Finally, it addresses a scenario where the option holder rescinds in the absence of the other party: if news reaches the other party within the option period, the rescission is valid; if after, the sale is already complete due to the option period expiring. This lesson shows the Hanafi emphasis on preventing harm (darar) as a basis for legal rulings.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): The right to annul or confirm a contract within a stipulated period.
من له الخيار (man lahu al-khiyar): The person who holds the right of option in a contract.
من لا خيار له (man la khayar lahu): The party in the contract who does not have the right of option.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or rescission of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa in this passage, why must the option holder inform the other party before rescinding the sale?
A) Because the contract is not binding until both parties know.
B) Because rescinding without notice causes harm to the other party.
C) Because the other party has a right to object to the rescission.
D) Because the option holder needs permission from the other party.

Key Takeaway
The option holder must inform the other party before rescinding to prevent harm; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
